Prophethood
beginner
5 min
The Necessity of Prophethood
Sanusi explains the necessity of sending messengers and the insufficiency of intellect.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the sending of messengers is necessary and why the intellect alone is insufficient for knowing moral obligations.

Core Idea
Without prophets, human reason cannot know right from wrong.

Sanusi begins a new chapter on prophethood by establishing that the sending of messengers is not only possible but necessary. He explains that while reason can know God's existence, it cannot determine moral obligations without divine revelation. This lesson explores why prophethood is among the contingent things we must believe in.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on prophethood
Read the Arabic passage slowly. Notice how Sanusi states that sending messengers is among the contingent things (jā'izāt) that must be believed.
The passage is concise; each word matters.
2
Understand the limitation of intellect
Sanusi says the intellect does not perceive obedience or disobedience without a revealed law. Reflect on why this is significant.
This is the key reason for the necessity of prophethood.
3
Ask: why must we believe in this?
Consider the implication: if intellect alone cannot know moral obligations, then without prophets, humans would have no guidance. This makes belief in prophethood mandatory.
This connects to the broader creed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل
في النبوات
ومِنَ الجائزاتِ ويجب الإيمانُ بهِ : بَعْثُ الرُّسُلِ إلى العبادِ ليبلغوهم أمر الله سبحانهُ ونهيه وإباحته ، وما يتعلَّقُ بذلكَ مِنْ خطابِ الوضع ؛ لما عرفت أنَّ العقلَ لا يُدرِكُ دون شرع طاعةً ولا معصية ولا ما بينهما
[ الكلام على المعجزة ]
وتفضَّلَ سبحانَهُ بتأييدهم بالمعجزة الدالة على صدقهم ؛ وهي فعلُ الله سبحانه ، خارق للعادة ، مُقارِنُ لدعوى الرسالة ، مُتحدّى بهِ قبل وقوعِهِ ، غيرُ مُكَذِّبِ
يُعجِزُ مَنْ يبغي معارضته عن الإتيان بمثلِهِ
•
فاحترزَ بالأَوَّلِ مِنَ القديمِ ، فليس فعلاً للهِ تعالى ، فلا يكون معجزةً ، ودخل فيه الفعل الذي تعلقت القدرة الحادثة بهِ ؛ كتلاوة النبيِّ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ القرآنَ ، فهو معجزةٌ لرسولِ اللهِ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ دونَ غيرِهِ ؛ إِذْ غيرُهُ
إذا تلاه إنَّما يحكيهِ ، وليس هو الآخذَ لَهُ عنِ المَلَكِ . ودخلَ ما لا تتعلَّقُ بهِ القدرة الحادثة ؛ كإحياء الموتى
Chapter on Prophethoods. And among the contingent things that must be believed in is the sending of messengers to servants to convey to them the command of Allah, His prohibition, and His permission, and what pertains to that of prescriptive speech; because you have known that the intellect does not perceive, without a revealed law, obedience nor disobedience nor what is between them. [Discussion on the Miracle] And He, glorified, favored by supporting them with the miracle that indicates their truthfulness; and it is an act of Allah, the glorified, that breaks the norm, is concurrent with the claim of prophethood, is a challenge before its occurrence, and is not contradicted; it incapacitates anyone who seeks to oppose it from producing the like of it. So, by the first [condition] he excluded the eternal, for it is not an act of Allah, so it is not a miracle; and included in it an act to which temporal power is attached, such as the Prophet's (peace and blessings be upon him) recitation of the Qur'an, for it is a miracle for the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) but not for others; since others, when they recite it, only narrate it and are not the ones who received it from the angel. And it includes what temporal power is not attached to, such as reviving the dead.
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This passage is a definition and explanation of prophethood and miracles. It begins with a new chapter: 'On Prophethoods'. Sanusi states that the sending of messengers is among the contingent possibilities (jā'izāt) that must be believed. The reason given is that the intellect alone cannot know obedience, disobedience, or intermediate matters without a revealed law. Then, under the heading 'Discussion on the Miracle', he explains that God supports prophets with miracles (mu'jiza) that prove their truthfulness. The definition of a miracle is given as an act of Allah that is extraordinary (khāriq li-l-'āda), concurrent with the claim of prophethood, issued as a challenge before its occurrence, and is not contradicted (i.e., it incapacitates anyone who wants to oppose it from producing the like). Then Sanusi explains the first condition ('act of Allah'): it excludes the eternal (al-qadīm) because that is not an act of Allah, so it cannot be a miracle. It includes acts to which temporal power (al-qudra al-ḥāditha) is attached, e.g., the Prophet's recitation of the Quran – that is a miracle for him but not for others, because others merely narrate it and did not receive it from the angel. It also includes acts to which temporal power is not attached, like reviving the dead.

Key Terms
نبوة
جائزات
رسول

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that human reason alone can determine all moral obligations without revelation.
Correction: Sanusi clarifies that the intellect cannot perceive obedience or disobedience without a revealed law, thus prophethood is necessary.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, why must we believe in the sending of messengers?
A) Because it is rationally impossible to know God without them.
B) Because the intellect cannot know moral obligations without a revealed law.
C) Because miracles prove their truth.
D) Because all people are born believers.

Key Takeaway
Prophethood is necessary because human reason alone cannot determine moral duties without divine revelation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a moral decision, which do you instinctively trust more: your own reasoning or the clear commands of Allah as delivered by His prophets? What does your answer reveal about your reliance on revelation?
?
If the intellect alone cannot even distinguish obedience from disobedience, how seriously do you take the daily recitation and study of the Qur'an and the Prophet's example? Is there a command you have habitually neglected because your reason deemed it unimportant or outdated?
?
This lesson states that without revelation, the intellect is blind to moral categories. How does that truth challenge your pride in your own intelligence? What step will you take this week to actively submit your reasoning to divine guidance?

The Definition and Conditions of a Miracle
Sanusi defines miracles and explains the first condition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the precise definition of a miracle (mu'jiza) and its conditions, especially the first condition that it is an act of Allah.

Core Idea
A miracle is an extraordinary act of God that proves a prophet's truth.

Having established the necessity of prophethood, Sanusi now explains how God supports prophets with miracles. He provides a precise definition with several conditions, and then elaborates on the first condition—that a miracle must be an act of Allah—distinguishing it from eternal matters and explaining examples like the Quran recitation.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition of a miracle
Read the Arabic definition carefully. Note each condition: act of Allah, extraordinary, concurrent with claim, challenge before occurrence, not contradicted, incapacitates opposition.
This is the core definition of mu'jiza.
2
Identify the six conditions
List the six conditions from the definition. They are: فعل الله, خارق للعادة, مقارن لدعوى الرسالة, متحدى به قبل وقوعه, غير مكذب, يعجز من يبغي معارضته عن الإتيان بمثله.
The last condition is sometimes considered part of the definition.
3
Understand the first condition in detail
Sanusi explains that 'act of Allah' excludes eternal things and includes acts with temporal power (like Quran recitation) and without (like reviving the dead).
This clarifies that miracles are divine acts, not human.
4
Apply the first condition to the Quran example
The Prophet's recitation of the Quran is a miracle for him because he received it from the angel; others only narrate it.
This shows how the condition works in practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

في النبوات

[ الكلام على المعجزة ]
وتفضَّلَ سبحانَهُ بتأييدهم بالمعجزة الدالة على صدقهم ؛ وهي فعلُ الله سبحانه ، خارق للعادة ، مُقارِنُ لدعوى الرسالة ، مُتحدّى بهِ قبل وقوعِهِ ، غيرُ مُكَذِّبِ
يُعجِزُ مَنْ يبغي معارضته عن الإتيان بمثلِهِ

Chapter on Prophethoods. And among the contingent things that must be believed in is the sending of messengers to servants to convey to them the command of Allah, His prohibition, and His permission, and what pertains to that of prescriptive speech; because you have known that the intellect does not perceive, without a revealed law, obedience nor disobedience nor what is between them. [Discussion on the Miracle] And He, glorified, favored by supporting them with the miracle that indicates their truthfulness; and it is an act of Allah, the glorified, that breaks the norm, is concurrent with the claim of prophethood, is a challenge before its occurrence, and is not contradicted; it incapacitates anyone who seeks to oppose it from producing the like of it. So, by the first [condition] he excluded the eternal, for it is not an act of Allah, so it is not a miracle; and included in it an act to which temporal power is attached, such as the Prophet's (peace and blessings be upon him) recitation of the Qur'an, for it is a miracle for the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) but not for others; since others, when they recite it, only narrate it and are not the ones who received it from the angel. And it includes what temporal power is not attached to, such as reviving the dead.

Commentary
This passage is a definition and explanation of prophethood and miracles. It begins with a new chapter: 'On Prophethoods'. Sanusi states that the sending of messengers is among the contingent possibilities (jā'izāt) that must be believed. The reason given is that the intellect alone cannot know obedience, disobedience, or intermediate matters without a revealed law. Checkpoint
Why is the recitation of the Quran a miracle for the Prophet but not for others?
A) Because others cannot recite as beautifully.
B) Because the Prophet received it from the angel, while others only narrate.
C) Because it is eternally miraculous.
D) Because it breaks the norm of nature.

Key Takeaway
A miracle is an act of Allah with specific conditions that confirm a prophet's truth; the first condition distinguishes it from eternal matters and includes both acts with and without temporal power.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever doubted the truth of a prophet because you thought miracles were just stories? How does Sanusi's definition challenge your skepticism? What would it mean for your faith if you truly accepted that the Quran is a miracle given to Muhammad (peace be upon him) as a divine act? Commit to reflecting on one miracle mentioned in the Quran today.
?
The miracle of the Quran is that it was recited by an unlettered prophet. Are you treating the Quran as a miracle in your life, or as just a book? What one change can you make today to honor it as divine?
?
If a miracle is an act of Allah that proves truth, what does it say about your own claim to follow the Prophet? Does your conviction rely on evidence or comfort? Take a moment to ask Allah to increase your certainty through reflection on His signs.

Prophethood

Introduction to Prophethood and the Necessity of Revelation
Sanusi transitions to the chapter on prophethood, establishing revelation as the source of obligation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that moral and legal obligations are known only through divine revelation, and that the sending of prophets is a necessary belief to convey that revelation.

Core Idea
Reason alone cannot know obedience or disobedience; revelation is required.

In this brief but pivotal passage, Sanusi wraps up a preceding argument and opens a new chapter on prophethood. He makes two critical points: all knowledge of obligation and prohibition comes from revelation, not reason; and sending messengers is an essential part of what we must believe about Allah. This lesson unpacks these foundational ideas.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation. Notice the shift from a concluding statement to a new chapter.
2
Identify the key epistemological claim
Focus on the statement that obligation and prohibition are known only after revelation comes. This is a foundational principle of Sunni theology.
3
Understand the content of prophethood
Note that sending messengers is listed among the 'possible things' that must be believed. The messengers convey Allah's commands, prohibitions, permissions, and prescriptive speech.
4
Reflect on the role of reason
The passage ends by asserting that reason alone cannot perceive obedience, disobedience, or intermediate categories. This justifies the need for revelation and prophets.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإذاً ؛ لم نعرف وجوبَ الإيمان ولا تحريم الكفران إلا بعد مجيء الشرع
فصل
في النبوات
ومِنَ الجائزاتِ ويجب الإيمانُ بهِ : بَعْثُ الرُّسُلِ إلى العبادِ ليبلغوهم أمر الله سبحانهُ ونهيه وإباحته ، وما يتعلَّقُ بذلكَ مِنْ خطابِ الوضع ؛ لما عرفت أنَّ العقلَ لا يُدرِكُ دون شرع طاعةً ولا معصية ولا ما بينهما
Thus, we do not know the obligation of faith nor the prohibition of disbelief except after the coming of revelation. Chapter on Prophethoods. And from among the possible things that must be believed in: the sending of messengers to people to convey to them the command of Allah, His prohibition, and His permission, and what relates to that of prescriptive speech (khiṭāb al-waḍʿ); because you have known that reason does not perceive, without revelation, any obedience, nor disobedience, nor what is between them.
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This passage is a transition and introduction to the chapter on prophethood. The author first concludes the previous discussion by stating that the obligation to believe and the prohibition of disbelief are only known through revelation, not through reason alone. He then opens a new chapter on prophethoods. He states that sending messengers is among the possible things (jāʾizāt) that must be believed about Allah. The messengers are sent to convey Allah's commands, prohibitions, and permissions, as well as prescriptive speech (khiṭāb al-waḍʿ) which includes legal classifications. The reason is that reason cannot independently discern obedience, disobedience, or intermediate categories without divine revelation. Thus, prophethood is necessary to communicate moral and legal obligations.

Key Terms
شرع
عقل
طاعة
معصية
بعث الرسل
خطاب الوضع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Human reason can independently determine right and wrong without divine revelation.
Correction: This passage states that reason does not perceive obedience or disobedience without revelation; therefore, revelation is necessary for moral knowledge.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, why is revelation necessary for knowing obligations?
A) Because reason is too weak to understand anything.
B) Because reason does not perceive obedience or disobedience without revelation.
C) Because prophets are needed to perform miracles.
D) Because Allah does not give reason to humans.

Key Takeaway
Without revelation, reason alone cannot determine moral and legal obligations; therefore, belief in the sending of prophets is essential.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If reason alone cannot tell you what obedience to Allah is, how do you know that your actions today are truly pleasing to Him? Are you relying on revelation—through the Qur'an and Sunnah—to guide every decision, or have you assumed some things are acceptable without checking? Commit to reviewing one daily act this week by asking: 'What does revelation say about this?'
?
The passage says we do not know the obligation of faith except after revelation. Have you ever felt that believing in Allah is 'obvious' and needs no prophetic guidance? How does that attitude undermine the very purpose for which prophets were sent? This week, thank Allah for sending you the revelation that made faith a clear obligation, and reflect on those who never received it.
?
Reason is blind to obedience and disobedience without revelation. Are there areas in your life where you rely on your own common sense rather than seeking religious knowledge? Identify one such area and take the first step to learn its ruling from the revealed sources.

Two types of miracles and the preference for the intellectual type
Sanusi discusses two types of miracles and states the superiority of the intellectual type.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinction between sensory and intellectual miracles and why the intellectual type, exemplified by the Qur'an, is preferred.

Core Idea
The greatest miracle is intellectual, not sensory.

Sanusi explains that while sensory miracles like multiplying food are well-known, some scholars specify that a true miracle must be of the intellectual type, exemplified by the Qur'an's unique composition. This passage clarifies the superiority of the intellectual miracle.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage slowly and then its English translation. Notice the examples given and the key terms.
2
Identify the two types of miracles
The passage mentions sensory miracles (like multiplying food) and then specifies the second type: intellectual (like the Qur'an's unique composition). Distinguish between them.
3
Understand the preference for the second type
Consider why some scholars argue that a miracle must be intellectual, as it is more apparent and not subject to sensory limitations.
The Prophet's knowledge of the Qur'an is also part of the miracle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتكثيرِ الطعام ، وانقيادِ الشجرِ ، ونحو ذلك ، وعَيَّنَ بعضُ أصحابنا في المعجزة : أن تكونَ مِنَ النوع الثاني لا الأَوَّلِ فتكون معجزة القرآن على هذا في نظمه المخصوص ، وإطلاع النبيِّ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ على ذلك دون سائر الناس ، وكلا الأمرين ليسَ مِنْ فعله ولا كسبه ، وهذا الثاني أظهرُ ، والله تعالى أعلم .
And the multiplication of food, and the subjugation of trees, and the like of that. And some of our companions specified concerning the miracle that it must be of the second type, not the first, so the miracle of the Qur'an according to this is in its specific composition, and the Prophet's (peace and blessings of Allah be upon him) knowledge of that to the exclusion of other people. And both matters are not from his action nor his acquisition. And this second is more apparent, and Allah Almighty knows best.
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This passage continues a discussion on the nature of miracles (mu'jizāt). It mentions examples of sensory miracles like multiplying food and trees bowing. Some scholars (أصحابنا) specify that a miracle must be of the second type (intellectual, such as the Qur'an's inimitability) rather than the first (sensory). The miracle of the Qur'an is thus its unique composition (نظمه المخصوص) and the Prophet's knowledge of it, which others do not possess. Both the miracle and the knowledge are not acts of the Prophet nor his acquisition (كسب). The author states that the second type (intellectual) is more apparent (أظهر).

Key Terms
معجزة
النوع الثاني
نظم
إطلاع
كسب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that miracles are only sensory events, like the splitting of the moon or multiplication of food.
Correction: This passage clarifies that intellectual miracles, such as the Qur'an's inimitability, are also considered miracles and are actually superior.

Checkpoint
What is the 'second type' of miracle mentioned in this passage?
A) Sensory miracles like multiplying food
B) Intellectual miracles like the Qur'an's composition
C) Miracles performed by saints
D) Miracles that occur after the prophet's death

Key Takeaway
The intellectual miracle of the Qur'an, with its unique composition and prophetic knowledge, is more apparent and superior as a proof of prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just learned that the intellectual miracle of the Qur'an is more apparent than sensory miracles. Has your own engagement with the Qur'an been more about its sensory appeal (voice, beauty) or its intellectual depth? How does that impact your conviction in prophethood?
?
The passage says the Prophet's knowledge of the Qur'an is not from his own acquisition but a divine grant. In what ways do you rely on your own knowledge and abilities versus relying on Allah's grant? Are there areas where you need to humble yourself and acknowledge that true guidance comes only from Him?
?
If the Qur'an's miracle is in its composition and prophetic knowledge, how does that challenge you to approach the Qur'an differently? What specific step can you take this week to engage with its unique composition and deepen your faith?

Prophethood
intermediate
4 min
Objection and Answer: Challenge by Inaction
Sanusi addresses an objection about challenging by not acting and provides an answer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the definition of miracle accommodates prophecies of non-action.

Core Idea
A miracle can be a predicted non-event if the knowledge of it is from Allah.

This lesson presents an objection to the standard definition of miracle as an act of Allah. The objector points out that prophets sometimes challenge by promising that something will not happen. The answer clarifies that the miracle lies in the prophetic knowledge and its fulfillment, which is itself an act of Allah. Some scholars even added a phrase to the definition to cover such cases.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
Read the objection introduced by 'فإن قلت' (if you say). Note the examples: Prophet Muhammad's statement 'My Lord has protected me' and Noah's challenge in the Quran. The objection argues that a miracle can be a challenge by non-action.
The key phrase is 'تحدي بعدم الفعل' (challenge by inaction).
2
Grasp the answer
Read the answer starting with 'فالجواب'. The miracle is identified as the prophet's knowledge and his informing of the outcome in accordance with what appeared. This knowledge is itself an act of Allah, created for the prophet.
The miracle is not the non-action per se but the divine knowledge and its realization.
3
Note the modification
Some scholars accepted the objection and added to the definition of miracle the phrase 'or what takes its place' (أو ما يقوم مقامه) to explicitly include cases of non-action.
This shows the flexibility of theological definitions in response to valid objections.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قلت : قد يتحدَّى النبيُّ بعدم الفعل ، كما قال عليهِ الصلاةُ والسلام : ( قَدْ عَصَمَنِي رَبِّي ) ، وكما قال نوح عليه السلامُ : ﴿ ثُمَّ أَقْضُواْ إِلَى وَلَا تُنظِرُونِ﴾ [يونس : ٧١] ، فقد وقع التحدي بعدم وقوع الفعل كالضرب والقتل . فالجواب : أَنَّ علمَهُ وإخبارَهُ بذلكَ على وَفْقِ ما ظهرَ . المعجزةُ ، وهو فعل الله خلقَهُ لهُ ، ومنهم مَنْ قَبِلَ هذا الاعتراض، فزادَ لإدخالِ ما ورد بعد قوله في شروط المعجزة : ( وهو فعل الله تعالى ( فقال : ( أو ما يقومُ مَقامَهُ ) .
For if you say: The prophet may challenge by [promising] non-action, as he (peace and blessings be upon him) said: 'My Lord has protected me,' and as Noah (peace be upon him) said: 'Then carry out your plan and do not give me respite' [Yunus 71]. So the challenge occurred by the non-occurrence of the act, like striking and killing. The answer: That his knowledge and his informing of that in accordance with what appeared is the miracle, and it is an act of Allah, He created it for him. And among them is one who accepted this objection, so he added, to include what occurred after his saying in the conditions of the miracle: 'and it is an act of Allah Almighty,' so he said: 'or what takes its place.'
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This passage presents an objection (فإن قلت) to a definition of miracle. The objector argues that sometimes a prophet challenges by promising that something will not happen (e.g., being protected from harm), as in the Prophet Muhammad's statement 'My Lord has protected me' and Noah's verse. The challenge is by the non-occurrence of an act, so how is this a miracle? The answer (فالجواب) is that the prophet's knowledge and his informing of that outcome in accordance with what appears is the miracle itself. This knowledge is an act of Allah created for him. Some scholars accepted this objection and added to the definition of miracle the phrase 'or what takes its place' (أو ما يقوم مقامه) to include such cases.

Key Terms
تحدي
عدم الفعل
علم
إخبار
خلق
ما يقوم مقامه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A miracle must always be a positive event (something happening).
Correction: This passage shows that a predicted non-event can also be a miracle if the prophetic knowledge of its occurrence is divinely given and comes true.

Checkpoint
According to the answer given, what constitutes the miracle when a prophet challenges by non-action?
A) The act of protection itself
B) The prophet's knowledge and information of the outcome
C) The fact that the enemy failed to act
D) The prophet's statement alone

Key Takeaway
A miracle can be a predicted non-event when the knowledge of its occurrence is divinely given and fulfilled.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a situation where you desperately want a visible sign from Allah, do you stop to consider that the real miracle might be the quiet divine knowledge He has already given you? How can you train yourself to trust in that unseen knowledge today?
?

?
If Allah can protect prophets through a predicted non-miracle, what does that mean for your own fears about the future? Are you willing to trade your anxiety for faith that Allah's knowledge of your tomorrow is sufficient?

Why Miracles Must Be Supernatural
Sanusi explains the condition 'kharq li'l-ada' and distinguishes miracles from ordinary events.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the condition 'kharq li'l-ada' (supernatural) is essential for miracles and how it excludes ordinary events, magic, and natural properties.

Core Idea
Miracles must break natural laws; ordinary events cannot prove prophethood.

Sanusi now adds a crucial condition to the definition of a miracle: it must be supernatural. Without this condition, any ordinary event could be mistaken for a miracle. This passage clarifies what counts as ordinary and why magic and natural properties do not qualify.

Guided Path
1
Understand the term 'kharq li'l-ada'
Start by noting that 'kharq li'l-ada' means 'supernatural' or 'breaking the usual course of things.' Sanusi uses this term to guard against ordinary events.
This is the key condition that distinguishes miracles from everyday occurrences.
2
Distinguish miracles from ordinary events
The passage states that ordinary events can be performed by both truthful and false claimants, so they cannot authenticate prophethood. Miracles must be unique to the truthful.
This is why the supernatural condition is necessary.
3
Examine the examples of ordinary events
Sanusi lists magic and natural properties (like magnetism) as ordinary. Even if rare, they have causes and thus are not supernatural.
Some might think magic is supernatural, but it has a specific cause, so it is still ordinary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واحترزَ بقولِهِ : ( خارق للعادة ) مِنَ المعتادِ ؛ فَإِنَّهُ يستوي فيه الصادقُ والكاذبُ ، ومِنَ المعتادِ : السحر ونحوه ، وإنْ كانَ سببُهُ العادي نادراً ، خلافاً لمَنْ جعل السحر خارقاً لكن بسببٍ خاص بهِ ، ومِنَ المعتادِ أيضاً : ما يُوجَدُ في بعض الأجسامِ مِنَ الخواص ؛ كجذب الحديدِ بحجر المغناطيس
And he guarded by his saying: 'supernatural' from the ordinary; for indeed the truthful and the false are equal in it. And from the ordinary are magic and the like, even if its usual cause is rare, contrary to those who made magic supernatural but due to a specific cause. And from the ordinary also are the properties found in some bodies, like the attraction of iron by the magnet stone.
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This passage explains why the condition 'supernatural' (خارق للعادة) is included in the definition of miracle. The term 'guarded' (احترز) means that this condition excludes ordinary events (المعتاد). In ordinary events, both the truthful and the false claimant can produce them, so they cannot serve as evidence. Examples of ordinary events include magic (سحر) and natural properties (خواص) like magnetism. Some consider magic supernatural, but the author refutes this, noting that magic has its own special cause and thus is not truly supernatural. The point is that miracles must break natural laws; otherwise, they would not be distinctive.

Key Terms
خارق للعادة
معتاد
سحر
خواص
مغناطيس

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That magic is a miracle because it seems supernatural.
Correction: Magic is actually ordinary because it has a specific cause, even if hidden. Miracles must have no natural cause.

Checkpoint
Why is the condition 'supernatural' (kharq li'l-ada) important for miracles?
A) Because ordinary events can be performed by anyone
B) Because magic is always supernatural
C) Because natural properties are also supernatural
D) Because miracles must be visible to all

Key Takeaway
A miracle must be supernatural, breaking natural laws, because ordinary events can be performed by both truthful and false claimants and thus cannot prove prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
If only clear supernatural breaks in nature can confirm prophethood, how seriously do you take the miracles of the Quran and the Prophet Muhammad (SAW) as proofs? Does this lesson move you from passive belief to a deeper, more active conviction that demands a response in your daily life?

Two Conditions for a Valid Miracle
Sanusi defines two conditions for a miracle: concurrent with claim and challenged before occurrence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two essential conditions that define a true miracle: it must accompany a prophetic claim and be challenged before its occurrence.

Core Idea
A miracle must be both linked to a prophetic claim and preceded by a challenge.

Sanusi now clarifies two critical conditions that distinguish a true miracle from other extraordinary events. Without these conditions, an event may be a saintly wonder or a preparatory sign, but not a miracle of prophethood. Let's examine each condition as Sanusi explains them in the passage below.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation to grasp the author's meaning.
Notice the precise wording: 'مقارن لدعوى الرسالة' and 'متحدى به قبل وقوعه'.
2
Identify the first condition
The first condition is that the miracle must be concurrent with the claim of prophethood. This excludes events without a claim or with a claim other than prophethood (e.g., sainthood).
Ask yourself: Does this event accompany a claim to be a prophet?
3
Identify the second condition
The second condition is that the miracle must be challenged before it occurs. The prophet must announce in advance that a specific event will be a sign of his truthfulness.
This excludes events that occur without a challenge (like irhas) or if the challenge is after the event.
4
Reflect on what is excluded
Consider examples that fail these conditions: an event without a claim (not a miracle), an event from a saint (ولاية), an event without prior challenge (إرهاص), or a challenge after the event.
These exclusions help define the boundaries of miracles.
5
Test your understanding
Answer the checkpoint question to ensure you can apply the conditions to distinguish a true miracle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبقوله : ( مُقارِنٌ لدعوى الرسالة ) مما وقع بدونِ دعوى ، أو بدعوى غير دعوى الرسالة ؛ كدعوى الولاية . وبقوله : ( مُتحدّى بهِ قبلَ وقوعِهِ ) أي : يقولُ : آيةً صدقي كذا ، مما وقع بدونِ تحديه ؛ كالإرهاص ونحوِهِ أو تحدّى بهِ لكن بعد وجودِهِ
And by his saying: 'concurrent with the claim of prophethood' excludes what occurs without a claim, or with a claim other than the claim of prophethood, like the claim of sainthood. And by his saying: 'challenged with it before its occurrence' means that he says: 'a sign of my truthfulness is such-and-such', excluding what occurs without his challenge, like the irhas (preparatory signs) and the like, or he challenges with it but after its existence.
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage explains two conditions for a miracle. First, 'concurrent with the claim of prophethood' (مقارن لدعوى الرسالة): This excludes events that occur without any claim, or with a claim other than prophethood (like sainthood, ولاية). A miracle must directly support a prophetic claim. Second, 'challenged with it before its occurrence' (متحدى به قبل وقوعه): The prophet must explicitly state in advance that this specific event will be a sign of his truthfulness. This excludes events that occur without a challenge (like irhas, preparatory signs before prophethood) or if the challenge is issued after the event has already occurred.

Key Terms
مقارن لدعوى الرسالة
متحدى به قبل وقوعه
ولاية
إرهاص

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think any extraordinary event from a prophet is automatically a miracle.
Correction: A true miracle must satisfy two conditions: it must accompany a prophetic claim and be challenged before its occurrence. Otherwise, it may be a saintly wonder (karama) or a preparatory sign (irhas).

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi's conditions, which of the following is NOT a valid miracle?
A) A prophet says 'If I am truthful, this tree will speak' and it speaks.
B) A prophet says 'This tree will speak' and it speaks without prior challenge.
C) A prophet says 'This tree will speak' after it has already spoken.
D) A prophet says 'This tree will speak' and it speaks as predicted.

Key Takeaway
A true miracle must be concurrent with the claim of prophethood and preceded by a challenge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The lesson teaches that a miracle must be tied to a prophetic claim. Is your certainty in the Prophet ﷺ built on the clear signs he brought, or on something less solid? What would it mean for your faith if you were to accept a sign that does not meet these conditions?
?
Imagine you are a prophet’s follower and you see an extraordinary event that happens without any prior challenge. Would you be tempted to consider it a miracle? This lesson forces you to recognize that even extraordinary things can be from sources other than prophethood. How does this discipline your heart from rushing to believe every wonder?
?
The condition of a challenge before the miracle means the prophet stakes his honor on what will happen. Have you ever committed yourself to a truth publicly before seeing the outcome? This lesson calls you to that same level of conviction. Are you willing to stand by the truth even before you see the sign, based on what Allah has already revealed?

Can a Miracle Occur After a Prophet's Death?
Sanusi presents two opinions on delaying a miracle after a prophet's death.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scholarly disagreement on whether a prophet's miracle can occur after his death and the reasoning behind the stronger opinion that it cannot.

Core Idea
A miracle after a prophet's death serves no purpose in confirming his message.

This lesson examines a specific question in the theology of prophethood: can a miracle be delayed until after the prophet's death? The great scholars al-Ash'ari and al-Baqillani weighed in, and their reasoning hinges on the purpose of miracles—to attest to the truthfulness of the prophet during his lifetime. The passage below presents the two views and the argument for the more apparent position.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the English translation. Let the author's rhythm and wording come through.
2
Identify the two opinions
Notice that al-Ash'ari had two opinions on this issue. Al-Baqillani held the second one, which is considered more apparent. What is the second opinion?
The second opinion is that it is not permissible to delay the miracle after death.
3
Understand the reasoning
The passage gives a reason for preferring the second opinion: preservation of the prophet's rulings during his lifetime provides no motive to receive them from him after death. Ask yourself: why does that matter?
Miracles are meant to confirm truthfulness; after the message is established, a later miracle adds nothing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهل يجوز تأخيرُ المعجزة عن موته؟ قولان للأشعري ، وقال بالثاني القاضي أبو بكر الباقلاني ، وهو الظاهرُ ، فإنَّ حفظَ ما نص عليهِ مِنْ أحكام شرعِهِ في حياتِهِ لا باعث على تلقيه منه
And is it permissible to delay the miracle until after his death? Two opinions from al-Ash'ari. And al-Qadi Abu Bakr al-Baqillani held the second, and it is the apparent one, for the preservation of what he prescribed from the rulings of his law during his lifetime provides no motive to receive it from him [after death].
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage addresses a specific question: Can a miracle occur after the death of a prophet? Imam al-Ash'ari had two opinions on this. The second opinion, held by al-Baqillani and deemed more apparent (الظاهر), says it is not permissible. The reason given is that if the prophet's rulings have already been preserved and conveyed during his lifetime, there is no cause (لا باعث) to receive them from him after death. A miracle after death would serve no purpose in confirming his truthfulness, as his message has already been established.

Key Terms
تأخير المعجزة
موت النبي
الأشعري
الباقلاني
باعث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A miracle can occur after a prophet's death just as during his lifetime.
Correction: The stronger scholarly opinion holds that delaying a miracle after death is not permissible because it would serve no purpose in confirming his truthfulness, as the message has already been established.

Checkpoint
According to the apparent opinion of al-Baqillani, why is delaying a miracle after death not permissible?
A) Because miracles are impossible after death
B) Because there is no motive to receive rulings after the prophet's death
C) Because only saints can perform miracles after death
D) Because the Qur'an is the only miracle needed

Key Takeaway
The majority of scholars (the apparent position) hold that miracles are tied to the prophet's lifetime and cannot be delayed after death because the purpose of confirming his message is already fulfilled.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Why do you rely on the truth of the Prophet Muhammad's message? Is it because of miracles you have witnessed, or because the message itself has been preserved and transmitted? How does this lesson affect your confidence in the preservation of the Qur'an and Sunnah?
?
If a miracle could occur after a prophet's death, would you feel more certain of his truthfulness? Reflect on the reason Sanusi gives: there is no motive to receive rulings from him after death. Does your heart seek extra signs beyond what has already been given?
?
The preservation of the prophet's rulings during his lifetime is enough to establish his message. How does this truth liberate you from constantly seeking new proofs? Take a moment to thank Allah for preserving the religion and commit to studying the preserved sources more deeply.

Condition of Non-Contradiction in Miracles
Sanusi explains the condition that a miracle must not contradict the claim, with examples and opinions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the condition that a miracle must not contradict the prophetic claim, and how scholars analyze ambiguous cases.

Core Idea
A miracle must align with the claim; contradiction invalidates it.

Sanusi now explains a crucial condition for miracles: they must not contradict the prophet's claim. He illustrates with a vivid example—a speaking hand that denies the prophet—and then addresses a debated scenario involving a revived dead person. This lesson clarifies when an extraordinary event qualifies as a miracle and when it does not.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Note the key term 'غير مكذب' (non-contradictory).
The passage uses a bracket notation; don't let it distract you.
2
Understand the core condition with the hand example
Identify how the hand speaking in contradiction invalidates the claim. Ask yourself: why does this event not count as a miracle?
3
Consider the debated case of the revived dead person
Notice that al-Qadi and Imam al-Haramayn had two opinions on whether contradiction from a revived dead person invalidates the miracle. Reflect on why this case is different from the hand example.
4
Analyze the later scholars' opinion
Some later scholars argued that the hand's contradiction does not invalidate the miracle because the challenge was only for the hand to speak, not to affirm the prophet. Understand the reasoning: the condition of non-contradiction is nuanced.
5
Reflect on the nuance
Consider how this condition protects the integrity of prophetic claims. Not every associated event is a miracle; it must be consistent with the claim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبقولِهِ : ( غيرُ مُكذِّب ( ممَّا إذا قالَ : آيةً صدقي : أنْ يُنطِقَ الله تعالى يدي ، فنطقَتْ بتكذيبه ، وفي تكذيب الميت المتحدَّى بإحيائِهِ قولان للقاضي وإمام الحرمين ، واختار أيضاً بعضُ المتأخّرينَ عدم القدح في تكذيب اليدِ و شبهها ؛ لعدم التحدي بتصديقها
And by his saying: 'non-contradictory' excludes the case when he says: 'A sign of my truthfulness is that Allah makes my hand speak,' but it speaks contradicting him. And concerning the contradiction of the dead person challenged with his revival, there are two opinions of al-Qadi and Imam al-Haramayn. And some later scholars also chose that there is no defect in the contradiction of the hand and the like, because there was no challenge for its affirmation.
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage explains the condition that a miracle must not contradict (غير مكذب) the prophetic claim. For example, if a prophet says 'Allah will make my hand speak as a sign of my truthfulness,' but the hand speaks to deny him, that event is not a valid miracle—it would contradict the claim. The text then discusses a special case: if a dead person is challenged to be revived, and the revived person contradicts the prophet. Al-Qadi (al-Baqillani) and Imam al-Haramayn (al-Juwayni) have two opinions. Some later scholars hold that such contradiction (e.g., from a speaking hand) does not invalidate the miracle because the challenge was not for the hand to affirm the prophet; it was only for the event to occur. The condition of non-contradiction is thus nuanced.

Key Terms
غير مكذب
تكذيب
يد
ميت
القاضي
إمام الحرمين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Any extraordinary event that occurs in connection with a prophet is automatically a miracle.
Correction: For an event to be a miracle, it must not contradict the prophet's claim; if it does, it invalidates the claim.

Checkpoint
According to some later scholars, why does a hand speaking in contradiction not invalidate the miracle?
A) Because the hand is not a reliable witness
B) Because the challenge was not for the hand to affirm the prophet
C) Because the prophet can control the hand
D) Because the hand is not part of the challenge

Key Takeaway
A miracle must be consistent with the prophet's claim; if it contradicts, it is not a miracle.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever claimed something as a sign from Allah, only to realize it contradicted your initial claim? How will you now ensure your signs align with the truth?
?

?
Sanusi discusses a case where a dead person's contradiction might not invalidate the miracle. Are you ever tempted to accept a sign that contradicts your beliefs? How will you apply the condition of non-contradiction to protect your faith?

How Miracles Indicate Prophethood: Three Views
Sanusi lists three views on miracle indication and argues against liars.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three proposed ways a miracle indicates prophetic truthfulness, and why the first two make it impossible for a miracle to occur from a liar.

Core Idea
Miracles cannot come from liars because rational proof or divine truthfulness would be violated.

Sanusi introduces a key question in the proof of prophethood: how does a miracle show that a prophet is truthful? He presents three views—rational, conventional, and customary—but focuses on the first two to show that if a miracle indicates rationally or by convention, it is absolutely impossible for a liar to perform one. This lesson unpacks that argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation carefully. Notice the question and the three proposed views.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Identify the three views
Find the three types of indication: rational (عقلية), conventional (وضعية), and customary (عادية). Understand that the first two are the focus.
3
Understand the impossibility
Sanusi states that under the first two views, a miracle cannot occur from a liar. Ask yourself why that is.
This is the key claim.
4
Note the reasons
For the rational view, a miracle from a liar would violate rational proof. For the conventional view, it would make God’s report false. Write these reasons in your own words.
These are the two arguments.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهل دَلالةُ المعجزة على صدق الرسولِ دَلالة عقلية أو وضعيّةٌ ، أو عاديَّةٌ بحسَبِ القرائنِ ؟ أقوال . أما على الأوَّلين فيستحيلُ صدورها على يد الكاذب ؛ لما يلزم على الأَوَّلِ مِنْ نقضِ الدليل العقلي ، وعلى الثاني مِنَ الخُلْفِ في خبرِهِ جلَّ وعلا ؛ إذْ تصديق الكاذب كذب
And is the indication of the miracle of the truthfulness of the messenger a rational indication or a conventional one, or a customary one according to the circumstances? [There are] sayings. As for the first two, it is impossible for it to occur at the hand of a liar, due to what follows: on the first, the violation of the rational proof, and on the second, the breach in His (Exalted) report; for affirming a liar is a lie.
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage raises the question of how a miracle provides evidence for a prophet's truthfulness. Three views are mentioned: the indication is rational (عقلية), conventional (وضعية), or customary (عادية) depending on circumstances (قرائن). The author focuses on the first two: if the indication is rational or conventional, then it is impossible for a miracle to occur from a liar. For the rational view, a miracle on a liar would violate rational proof (نقض الدليل العقلي). For the conventional view, it would imply a breach in God's truthful report (الخلف في خبره), because God would be affirming a liar, which is a lie. This shows the importance of miracles as definitive proofs.

Key Terms
دلالة عقلية
دلالة وضعية
دلالة عادية
قرائن
نقض الدليل العقلي
خلف خبر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think miracles are merely customary events that could happen to anyone, even a liar.
Correction: This passage shows that if the indication is rational or conventional, miracles are impossible from liars, making them definitive proof of prophethood.

Checkpoint
According to the rational view of dalalah, why can't a miracle occur from a liar?
A) Because miracles are rare
B) Because it would violate a rational proof
C) Because liars cannot perform miracles
D) Because God does not allow it

Key Takeaway
Miracles serve as definitive proof of prophethood because under rational or conventional indication, a miracle from a liar is rationally or divinely impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If a miracle is an undeniable sign from God, why do you still hold back from fully committing to His messenger? What worldly attachments are you protecting by your hesitation?
?
The lesson states that affirming a liar is a lie. When have you, by your actions or silence, affirmed a falsehood about God or His religion? Will you repent and correct it today?
?
Rational proof cannot be violated. What intellectual doubts do you harbor about prophethood? What flawed reasoning keeps you from certainty? Are you willing to abandon that reasoning and submit to the truth?

The Habitual Indication of Miracles
Sanusi explains the third view that the indication is habitual and gives its proof and conclusion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the third view on how miracles indicate prophethood—the habitual indication—and why it yields certain knowledge.

Core Idea
Habitual indication gives necessary knowledge, which cannot coexist with falsehood.

Sanusi now presents the third and final view on the evidential force of miracles: that the indication is habitual (ʿādiyya), based on God's consistent practice. This view holds that when a miracle occurs, it produces necessary knowledge of the claimant's truthfulness, and that knowledge is so certain that it cannot be mistaken. In this passage, Sanusi lays out the proof and the evidence from God's custom.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once to get the flow. Then read the literal translation to ensure you grasp every element of the argument.
2
Identify the two parts of the proof
Notice how the passage first states the conditional (if the indication is habitual) and the result (necessary knowledge). Then it argues that this knowledge makes falsehood impossible, and finally cites God's custom as evidence.
The argument has a logical core and an empirical reinforcement.
3
Understand the impossibility
Consider why necessary knowledge cannot turn into ignorance. If we know with certainty that someone is truthful, it is impossible for them to be a liar—otherwise our knowledge would be false, which is self-contradictory.
This is a rational argument based on the definition of necessary knowledge.
4
Reflect on the role of God's custom
Sanusi adds that God has consistently prevented liars from performing miracles. This habitual pattern supports the reliability of miracles as signs of truthfulness.
The custom (ʿāda) is not a logical proof but a cumulative evidence from history.
5
Compare with other views
Think about how this habitual view differs from the rational and optional views. In all three, the conclusion is the same: miracles provide certain proof.
This lesson focuses only on the habitual view; a full comparison is covered elsewhere.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأَمَّا إِنْ قلنا : إنَّ دلالة المعجزة عادية بحسَب القرائن .. فحيثُ حصل العلم الضروري عنها بصدقِ الآتي بها فإنَّهُ يستحيلُ أنْ يكونَ كاذباً ، وإلا انقلب العلم الضروري جهلاً ، ولم يُجْرِ سبحانه وتعالى عادتَهُ مِنْ أَوَّلِ الدنيا إلى الآنَ إلا بعدم تمكين الكاذب مِنَ المعجزاتِ
And as for if we say that the indication of the miracle is habitual according to circumstances, then whenever necessary knowledge is obtained from it of the truthfulness of the one who brings it, it is impossible for him to be a liar; otherwise necessary knowledge would turn into ignorance. And the Exalted and Transcendent has not conducted His custom from the beginning of the world until now except by not enabling a liar with miracles.
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This passage completes the discussion of the three views by presenting the third view: the indication of a miracle is habitual (adiyya), meaning that it is based on God's regular practice ('ada). When a miracle occurs, it gives necessary knowledge (ilm daruri) that the claimant is truthful. If this knowledge is genuine, it is impossible for the person to be a liar, because that would turn necessary knowledge into ignorance, an absurdity. Additionally, God's custom throughout history has been not to enable liars to perform miracles. This habitual pattern reinforces the reliability of miracles as evidence. Thus, on all three views, miracles provide certain proof of prophethood.

Key Terms
دلالة عادية
العلم الضروري
عادة الله

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that habitual indication is weaker or less certain than rational indication.
Correction: Sanusi shows that habitual indication yields necessary knowledge, which is just as certain as rational knowledge. The difference lies in the source of the knowledge, not its certainty.

Checkpoint
According to the habitual view, what happens if a liar were to perform a miracle?
A) It would still be possible
B) Necessary knowledge would become ignorance, which is impossible
C) God's custom would change
D) The miracle would be reclassified

Key Takeaway
The habitual view holds that miracles give necessary knowledge of truthfulness, and God's custom prevents liars from performing them, making the evidence certain.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have been given necessary knowledge through the miracles of the prophets, especially the Quran. Have you ever allowed a fleeting doubt to creep in, effectively turning that necessary knowledge into ignorance? What does that say about your certainty in faith? Will you command your heart to return to that knowledge without hesitation?
?
God's custom has never allowed a liar to perform a miracle. Reflect on your own life: have you ever spoken falsely about God or His religion, expecting His support? How does this truth challenge you to be absolutely truthful in your words and beliefs, and to repent if you have been insincere?

Believing Prophets and Their Sinlessness
Sanusi explains the implications of prophetic truthfulness proven by miracles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why it is obligatory to believe everything the prophets brought and why sin is impossible for them both rationally and by divine law.

Core Idea
If prophets could sin, we would be commanded to sin – which is impossible.

Sanusi now draws the final conclusions from the proof of prophecy through miracles. Because miracles confirm the truthfulness of the prophets, we must accept everything they convey from God. Moreover, their status as role models requires that they be preserved from all sin, even from disliked acts. This lesson examines the rational and scriptural basis for prophetic infallibility.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the English translation to grasp the main points.
Notice the logical flow: from truthfulness to obligation to believe, then to impossibility of sin.
2
Identify the two main implications
Sanusi draws two implications: (1) we must believe everything prophets bring, (2) sin is impossible for them. Look for how he supports each.
3
Understand the rational argument for infallibility
Lying is impossible for prophets rationally because their truthfulness is already proven by miracles. Ask: why would lying contradict their truthfulness?
This is a rational necessity (wujub 'aqli).
4
Understand the legal argument for infallibility
Sins are impossible by sacred law because we are commanded to follow the prophets. If they could sin, we would be commanded to sin, but God does not command evil (Quran 7:28). This is a legal impossibility (istihalah shar'iyyah).
The passage also extends to disliked acts and certain permissible acts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا عُلِمَ صدقُ الرسلِ بدلالة المعجزة وجب تصديقهم في كل ما أتوا به عن الله تعالى. به فيما يستحيلُ على الأنبياء عليهم الصلاة والسلام ويستحيلُ منهم الكذب عقلاً، والمعاصي شرعاً؛ لأنَّنا مأمورونَ بالاقتداء بهم، فلو جازَتْ عليهم المعصية لكُنَّا مأمورينَ بها، ﴿ قُلْ إِنَّ اللَّهَ لَا يَأْمُرُ بِالْفَحْشَاءِ﴾ [الأعراف : ٢٨]، وبهذا تعرفُ عدم وقوع المكروه منهم أيضاً، بل والمباح على الوجه الذي يقعُ مِنْ غيرهم، وبالله تعالى التوفيق
And when the truthfulness of the messengers is known by the evidence of the miracle, it is obligatory to affirm them in everything they brought from God, Most High. By that, regarding what is impossible for the prophets, peace be upon them: lying is impossible for them rationally, and acts of disobedience are impossible for them by sacred law; because we are commanded to emulate them, and if sin were permissible for them, we would be commanded to do it. (And He said: Say: Indeed, Allah does not command immorality) [Quran 7:28]. And by this you know that disliked acts also do not occur from them, nor even permissible acts in the manner that they occur from others. And with Allah is success.
Source pages p. 112

Commentary
This passage concludes the section on prophethood by stating the implications of believing in the prophets based on miracles. Once their truthfulness is confirmed, we must believe everything they bring from God. Then it discusses the impossibility of sin for prophets: lying is impossible rationally (because it contradicts truthfulness), and sin is impossible by divine law (because we are commanded to follow them, and if they could sin, we would be commanded to sin, which is impossible). A Quranic verse is cited to support that God does not command evil. Moreover, even disliked acts and even permissible acts in a lowly manner do not occur from prophets; they are preserved from all that diminishes their status.

Key Terms
صدق الرسل
وجوب التصديق
العصمة
الأنبياء
الكذب عقلاً
المعاصي شرعاً

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think prophets can commit minor sins or forget things that do not affect their message.
Correction: Sanusi's argument shows that all sins, disliked acts, and even certain permissible acts are impossible for prophets because they are our perfect role models.

Checkpoint
Why are sins impossible for prophets according to Sanusi?
A) Because they are too holy
B) Because we are commanded to follow them, and if they could sin, we would be commanded to sin
C) Because miracles prove they cannot sin
D) Because they are angels

Key Takeaway
Prophets are infallible in conveying the message and in their actions; any sin would contradict their role as models for humanity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the Prophet never sinned, yet you excuse your own sins by saying 'I am not a prophet', are you not using his perfection as an excuse rather than a model? How will you change your view of emulation today?
?
The passage says we are commanded to emulate the prophets. Think of one sin you struggle with. If the Prophet never did it, how can you justify continuing? What step will you take this week to align your action with his example?
?
God does not command immorality (Quran 7:28). Yet you sometimes fall into sin. Does this verse accuse you of disobeying God's command? How will you repent and renew your intention to follow the prophetic model starting now?

Defending Miracles: Possibility Does Not Imply Actuality
Sanusi defends the reliability of miracles against the objection that miracles could appear on liars.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi defends the evidential value of miracles by distinguishing logical possibility from actual occurrence, and why a miracle on a liar does not undermine certainty.

Core Idea
Possibility does not imply actuality; a miracle on a liar is possible but never actual.

Sanusi addresses a critical objection about miracles: if a miracle can appear on a false prophet, how can we trust any miracle? This passage provides a precise rational defense by clarifying what 'possibility' truly means, and why the mere possibility of a miracle on a liar does not undermine the certainty of a true prophet's miracle.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice that Sanusi begins by mentioning Allah’s protection against sorcery, then raises a hypothetical objection about miracles on liars.
Pay attention to the logical flow from the objection to the response.
2
Identify the objection and response
The objection: if a miracle can appear on a liar, then no miracle proves truthfulness. Sanusi’s response: such a miracle would not produce knowledge; also, possibility does not imply actuality.
The key phrase is 'لا يلزم من جواز الشيء وقوعه'.
3
Understand the meaning of 'جواز'
Sanusi defines 'جواز' (permissibility) as: if a thing were to occur, no impossibility would follow from it in its essence. This is logical possibility, not actual occurrence.
Contrast this with 'وقوع' (actual occurrence).
4
Apply the principle to the miracle argument
Even if a miracle on a liar is logically possible, it does not happen in reality. The actual miracle of a true prophet remains certain, because possibility does not entail occurrence.
The example of the world’s non-existence illustrates this perfectly.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا خيَّل بسحرٍ ونحوِهِ أظهرَ اللهُ فضيحتَهُ عن قُرْبٍ ، فللَّهِ الحمد على معاملته في ذلك ونحوه بمخضِ الفضل والكرم . ويجوز أن تظهر المعجزة على يد الكاذب لو انخرقَتِ العادةُ ، ولا يحصل حينئذ بها علمُ صدقِهِ ، وإلا كانَ الجهلُ علماً ، وتجويز خرْقِ العادةِ عند حصولِ العلمِ بالصدق في حقِّ المحقِّ لا يقدح في العلم ؛ إذ لا يلزمُ مِنْ جواز الشيء وقوعه ، ألا ترى أَنَّا نُجوِّزُ استمرار عدم العالم معَ علمنا ضرورةً بوجودِهِ ؛ إذْ معنى الجواز : أَنَّهُ لو قُدِّرَ واقعاً لم يلزم منه محال لذاته ؛ لأنه محتمل الوقوع
And if he deludes with sorcery or the like, Allah exposes his disgrace quickly, so praise be to Allah for His dealing in that and the like with pure favor and generosity. And it is permissible that a miracle appear on the hand of a liar if custom were broken, and knowledge of his truthfulness does not occur then through it; otherwise ignorance would be knowledge. And the deeming permissible of breaking custom when knowledge of truthfulness has occurred in the case of the truthful does not detract from knowledge; for permissibility of a thing does not entail its occurrence. Do you not see that we deem permissible the continued non-existence of the world while we know by necessity its existence? For the meaning of permissibility is that if it were assumed to occur, no impossibility would follow from it in its essence, because it is possible of occurrence.
Source pages p. 112

Commentary
This passage is an argument defending the evidential value of miracles against a potential objection. The objector might say: if it is possible for a miracle to appear on a liar, then how can we trust any miracle as proof? Sanusi begins by noting that when a sorcerer creates illusions, Allah exposes him quickly – that is a kind of divine protection. Then he addresses the hypothetical: even if a miracle were to occur on the hand of a liar due to a break in custom, that would not produce knowledge of his truthfulness. If it did, then ignorance (doubt) would be knowledge, which is absurd. Moreover, the fact that we allow the possibility of custom-breaking in the case of a true prophet does not undermine our knowledge of his truthfulness, because possibility of something does not mean it actually happens. To illustrate, Sanusi gives a rational example: we can conceive of the world not existing (permissibility of its non-existence), yet we are absolutely certain of its existence. The meaning of 'permissible' here is that if it were to occur, no logical contradiction would follow. So the mere possibility of a miracle on a liar does not make the actual miracle of a true prophet unreliable. The argument follows a classic kalam method: it distinguishes between logical possibility and actual occurrence, preserving the certainty of knowledge derived from miracles.

Key Terms
معجزة
جواز
خرق العادة
علم
صدق
محال
وقوع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If a miracle can appear on a liar, then no miracle can prove truthfulness.
Correction: Sanusi explains that a miracle on a liar would not produce knowledge of his truthfulness, and possibility does not entail actuality. The actual miracle of a true prophet remains certain.

Checkpoint
What is the meaning of 'جواز' (permissibility) according to Sanusi in this passage?
A) That a thing is possible to occur
B) That if a thing were to occur, no impossibility would follow from it in itself
C) That a thing is actually occurring
D) That a thing is necessary

Key Takeaway
The possibility of a miracle on a liar does not make the miracle of a true prophet uncertain; possibility does not entail actuality.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When a doubt about a prophetic miracle enters your mind, do you confuse 'it is possible' with 'it is so'? How can you train yourself to distinguish between possibility and actuality in matters of faith?
?
Do you ever hesitate to accept a clear truth because you can imagine a hypothetical counterexample? What would change if you truly internalized that possibility does not entail actuality?
?
Reflect on your own certainty: Is your belief in the Prophet ﷺ based on logical possibilities or on the actual miracle that occurred? Which one gives you certainty? How does Sanusi's distinction guide you to hold firm against mere possibilities?

The Necessity of Believing Prophets and Their Impeccability
Sanusi establishes the obligation to believe prophets and their infallibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why it is obligatory to believe all that prophets bring and how their impeccability (ʿiṣma) is established rationally and legally.

Core Idea
Prophets must be believed in everything; they are protected from sin because we are commanded to follow them.

Sanusi builds on the previous lesson where truthfulness of prophets was established by miracles. Now he draws the necessary conclusion: we must affirm everything they convey. He then explains why prophets are infallible—lying is rationally impossible, and sins are legally impossible because following them would otherwise obligate sin.

Guided Path
1
Link miracle to belief
Read the first part of the passage: once a prophet's truthfulness is known via a miracle, it becomes obligatory to believe everything they bring from Allah. This is the foundation of prophetic authority.
Notice that the obligation is tied to the proof (miracle), not blind acceptance.
2
Identify the two impossibilities
Sanusi states that lying is impossible for prophets rationally (ʿaqlan) and sins are impossible by sacred law (sharʿan). Understand the difference: rational impossibility is inherent, legal impossibility is a divine prohibition.
3
Understand the proof for legal impeccability
Sanusi argues: because we are commanded to follow prophets, if they could sin, we would be commanded to sin—but Allah does not command indecency (Quran 7:28). This proves that sin is impossible for them by law.
This is a logical deduction based on the nature of divine command.
4
Extend to disliked and permissible acts
The passage concludes that not only sins, but also disliked acts (makrūh) and even permissible acts (mubāḥ) in the manner of non-prophets do not occur from prophets. This underscores their complete moral perfection.
Consider why even permissible acts are restricted—to maintain perfect example.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا عُلِمَ صدقُ الرسلِ بدلالة المعجزة وجب تصديقهم في كل ما أتوا به عن الله تعالى . بِهِ [ فيما يستحيلُ على الأنبياء عليهم الصلاة والسلام ] ويستحيلُ منهم الكذب عقلاً ، والمعاصي شرعاً ؛ لأنَّنا مأمورونَ بالاقتداء بهم ، فلو جازَتْ عليهم المعصية لكُنَّا مأمورينَ بها ، ﴿ قُلْ إِنَّ اللَّهَ لَا يَأْمُرُ بِالْفَحْشَاءِ﴾ [الأعراف : ۲۸] ، وبهذا تعرفُ عدم وقوع المكروه منهم أيضاً ، بل والمباح على الوجه الذي يقعُ مِنْ غيرهم ، وبالله تعالى التوفيق
And when the truthfulness of the messengers is known through the evidence of a miracle, it is obligatory to believe them in everything they have brought from Allah, the Exalted. [With regard to what is impossible for the prophets, peace be upon them:] Lying is impossible for them rationally, and sins are impossible for them by sacred law; because we are commanded to follow them, so if sin were possible for them, we would be commanded to commit it. [Allah says:] 'Say: Indeed Allah does not command indecency' [Quran 7:28]. And by this you know that disliked acts also do not occur from them, nor even permissible acts in the manner that they occur from others. And success is from Allah, the Exalted.
Source pages p. 112

Commentary
This passage combines two interconnected rulings. First, Sanusi states a fundamental principle: once a prophet's truthfulness is established by a miracle, it becomes obligatory to affirm everything they convey from Allah. This is the basis of prophetic authority. Then he turns to what is impossible for prophets. Two categories are distinguished: (1) Lying is impossible rationally (ʿaqlan) – a prophet cannot intentionally or unintentionally convey falsehood about divine matters because that would contradict the purpose of prophethood. (2) Sins are impossible by sacred law (sharʿan) – not inherently impossible rationally, but prohibited by divine command because we are commanded to follow them. The proof is logical: if sinning were possible for a prophet, then since we must follow them, we would be commanded to sin, but Allah does not command indecency. This verse from al-Aʿrāf is cited as confirmation. Sanusi extends this to also negate the occurrence of disliked acts (makrūh) and even permissible acts (mubāḥ) if they occur in the same manner as from non-prophets. This is a strong statement of prophetic infallibility (ʿiṣma). The passage ends with a prayer for divine success.

Key Terms
تصديق
رسل
معجزة
استحالة
كذب
معاصي
اقتداء
مكروه
مباح

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that prophets could commit minor sins unintentionally.
Correction: Sanusi explicitly states that sins are impossible by law, and even disliked or certain permissible acts in an improper way do not occur from them.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, what is the proof that sins are impossible for prophets by sacred law?
A) Because prophets are inherently sinless
B) Because sinning would contradict their miracles
C) Because we are commanded to follow them, so if they sinned, we would be commanded to sin
D) Because the Quran explicitly says they cannot sin

Key Takeaway
Prophets must be believed in all they convey, and they are infallible in both rational and legal senses.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You claim to follow the Prophet ﷺ, but do you truly accept everything he brought, or do you selectively follow what suits you? What area of your life are you ignoring his guidance?
?
If prophets are infallible and we are commanded to follow them, then every sin you commit is a failure to follow. How does this change your view of your own sins? Will you now strive more to imitate the Prophet in every detail, even the seemingly small matters?
?
The passage says even permissible acts do not occur from prophets in the same way as from others. This means they lived every moment intentionally for Allah. Can you say the same about your own permissible actions? How much of your daily routine is unconscious versus purposeful worship?
