The Quran's Inimitability as Proof of Prophethood
Sanusi enumerates the Quranic challenge stages and argues from Arab silence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi uses the Quran's inimitability and the Arabs' failure to meet its challenges as a proof of Muhammad's prophethood.

Core Idea
The Quran's inimitability is the ultimate proof of Muhammad's prophethood.

Sanusi begins by affirming that Muhammad's claim to prophethood is necessarily known, and he presented countless miracles, the greatest being the Quran. This passage shows how the Quran's eloquence challenged the Arabs, progressively demanding they produce similar speech, and their failure despite their pride confirms its divine origin.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage slowly, then the translation. Notice the rhetorical force of Sanusi's language.
The passage starts with a chapter heading on proving prophethood.
2
Identify the three stages of challenge
Locate the three Quranic verses Sanusi cites that progressively intensify the challenge: ten surahs, one surah, then total incapacity of all jinn and humans.
The verses are from Hud 13, al-Baqara 23, and al-Isra 88.
3
Reflect on the psychological argument
Sanusi highlights that the Arabs were naturally proud of their eloquence and quick to react, yet they remained silent. Ask yourself why their silence is significant.
This is a key point: their pride would have compelled them to respond if they could.
4
Connect to prophethood
Understand how this cumulative argument proves that the Quran is from Allah and thus Muhammad is a true prophet.
The failure to meet the challenge despite expertise shows divine origin.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل [ في بيانِ إثباتِ الرسالة لسيدنا محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم ] ونبينا ومولانا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ قد عُلِمَ ضرورة ادّعاؤُه الرسالة ، وتحدى بمعجزاتٍ لا يُحاط بها [ معجزة القرآن العظيم ] وأفضلُها القرآنُ العظيم الذي لم تزل تقرعُ أسماع البلغاء بتضليل كل دين غير الإسلام آياته ، وتُحرّك بطلب المعارضة على سبيل التعجيز حميَّةَ اللُّسْنِ المتوقدي الفطنة ، الأقوياء العارضة نظماً ونثراً ، الخائضين في كلِّ فن مِنْ فنونِ البلاغةِ طولاً وعرضاً ؛ بحيثُ لا تُفْلِتُ مِنْ معارضتهم أمنعُ كلمةٍ وإِنْ لم يُعرَّض فيها بعجزهم ، فكيفَ وهم يسمعونَ معون في تعجيزهم صريح قولِهِ تعالى : ﴿ فَأْتُواْ بِعَشْرِ سُوَرٍ مِثْلِهِ مُفْتَرَيَاتٍ ﴾ [هود : ١٣] ، ثم تنزَّلَ معهم فقال : ﴿ فَأْتُواْ بِسُورَةٍ مِّن مِثْلِهِ ﴾ [البقرة : ٢٣] ، ثم صرَّحَ بعجز الجميع ؛ جِنَّهُمْ وإنسهم ، مفترقين أو مجتمعين ، فقال : ﴿ قُل لَّئِنِ اجْتَمَعَتِ الإِنسُ وَالْجِنُّ عَلَى أَن يَأْتُوا بِمِثْلِ هَذَا الْقُرْءَانِ لَا يَأْتُونَ بِمِثْلِهِ، وَلَوْ كَانَ بَعْضُهُمْ لِبَعْضِ ظَهِيرًا ﴾ [الإسراء : ۸۸] ، ومع ذلك لم تتحرَّك أَنفَتُهم وهم المجبولونَ عليها ؟! ومِنْ عادتهم أنَّهم لا يتمالكونَ معَها ضبط أنفسهم عند ورودِ أدنى
Chapter [ on proving the prophethood of our master Muhammad, may Allah bless him and grant him peace ]. And our Prophet and Master Muhammad, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, his claim to prophethood is known necessarily, and he challenged with countless miracles. [The miracle of the Great Quran] And the greatest of them is the Great Quran, whose verses never cease to strike the ears of the eloquent, leading astray every religion other than Islam, and stirring up the pride of those with sharp intelligence, the strong in constructing poetry and prose, those who delve into every art of eloquence length and breadth, by demanding opposition by way of rendering them incapable, such that no word—even if no mention of their incapacity was made—escapes their opposition. So how [could they] when they hear clearly stated in their incapacitation the explicit saying of Allah, the Exalted: 'Then bring ten surahs like it, fabricated' [Hud 13]; then He descended (in demand) with them and said: 'Then bring a surah like it' [al-Baqara 23]; then He declared the incapacity of all: their jinn and humans, separate or together, saying: 'Say: If mankind and jinn gathered to produce the like of this Quran, they could not produce the like of it, even if they were helpers of one another' [al-Isra 88]. And despite that, their noses did not stir, while they are naturally disposed to pride? And it is their habit that they cannot control themselves with that pride upon the occurrence of the least...
Source pages p. 113

Commentary
This passage is an introduction to the proof of Muhammad's prophethood, focusing on the Quran as the greatest miracle. Sanusi begins by stating that Muhammad's claim to prophethood is known necessarily (darūra) – it is evident. He challenged with countless miracles, but the greatest is the Quran. He describes the Quran's effect: its verses continuously strike the ears of eloquent Arabs, refuting every non-Islamic religion, and challenging them to produce something similar. Sanusi emphasizes that the Quran challenged them despite their mastery of eloquent prose and poetry. The challenge was progressively intensified: first to produce ten surahs, then one surah, and finally a declaration that all of humanity and jinn together cannot produce its like. Yet, despite their natural pride and quickness to react, they did not respond. Sanusi notes that it is their habit that they cannot restrain themselves when faced with even a slight insult to their language, but here they remained silent. The passage ends mid-sentence at the page break, but the argument is clear: the Arabs' failure to respond to the challenge is evidence of the Quran's divine origin.

Key Terms
معجزة
القرآن
تحدٍ
إعجاز
بلاغة
معارضة
سورة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Quran's inimitability is only about its beautiful style, not a proof of prophethood.
Correction: Sanusi shows it is a proof because the Arabs, masters of eloquence, were unable to meet the challenge despite their pride, confirming divine origin.

Checkpoint
What three stages of challenge does Sanusi mention from the Quran?
A) Challenging to produce ten surahs, then one surah, then a single verse
B) Challenging to produce ten surahs, then one surah, then declaring total incapacity
C) Challenging to produce a book, then a surah, then a single word
D) Challenging to produce poetry, prose, then a sermon

Key Takeaway
The Arabs' failure to respond to the Quran's progressive challenge, despite their expertise and pride, proves the Quran is divine and Muhammad is a true prophet.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You claim the Quran is the word of Allah, yet do you live as if it is a living challenge that confronts your every assumption and habit, or have you reduced it to a book you merely recite?
?
The Arabs' pride kept them from admitting their inability. Where in your life is your pride silencing you from submitting to a clear truth from the Quran that would require a painful change?
?
The Quran's verses 'lead astray every religion other than Islam'—have you allowed the Quran to expose and dismantle the idols of your own heart, such as status, comfort, or self-reliance, or do you treat it as harmless?

The Quran's Inimitability: The Challenge and the Failure
Sanusi details the Quranic challenge and the Arabs' failure.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Quran's inimitability serves as a proof of Muhammad's prophethood, focusing on the challenge verses and the Arabs' inability to respond despite their pride.

Core Idea
The Arabs' silence in the face of the Quranic challenge proves its divine origin.

Sanusi begins by establishing that the Quran is the greatest miracle of the Prophet. He describes how the Quran's verses challenged the eloquent Arabs to produce something similar, yet they remained silent despite their extreme pride. This lesson examines that challenge and the two scholarly explanations for their failure.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the Quranic challenge
Read the Arabic passage that describes the Quran's verses striking the ears of the eloquent and the three challenge verses. Notice how Sanusi emphasizes the Arabs' natural pride.
The challenge progresses from ten surahs to one surah to a collective impossibility.
2
Understand the psychological barrier
Reflect on why the Arabs' pride did not move them to respond, given their usual sensitivity to any disparagement. This highlights the supernatural nature of the Quran.
3
Learn the two opinions on their failure
Sanusi presents two explanations: incapacity (al-ashah) and sarfah (turning away). Understand the difference and which is more correct according to him.
Sarfah means Allah removed their ability or desire to challenge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل
[ في بيانِ إثباتِ الرسالة لسيدنا محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم ]
ونبينا ومولانا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ قد عُلِمَ ضرورة ادّعاؤُه الرسالة ، وتحدى بمعجزاتٍ لا يُحاط بها
[ معجزة القرآن العظيم ]
وأفضلُها القرآنُ العظيم الذي لم تزل تقرعُ أسماع البلغاء بتضليل كل دين غير الإسلام آياته ، وتُحرّك بطلب المعارضة على سبيل التعجيز حميَّةَ اللُّسْنِ المتوقدي الفطنة ، الأقوياء العارضة نظماً ونثراً ، الخائضين في كلِّ فن مِنْ فنونِ البلاغةِ طولاً وعرضاً ؛ بحيثُ لا تُفْلِتُ مِنْ معارضتهم أمنعُ كلمةٍ وإِنْ لم يُعرَّض فيها بعجزهم ، فكيفَ وهم يسمعونَ معون [؟] في تعجيزهم صريح قولِهِ تعالى : ﴿ فَأْتُواْ بِعَشْرِ سُوَرٍ مِثْلِهِ مُفْتَرَيَتِ ﴾ [هود : ١٣] ، ثم تنزَّلَ معهم فقال : ﴿ فَأْتُواْ بِسُورَةٍ مِّن مِثْلِهِ ﴾ [البقرة : ٢٣] ، ثم صرَّحَ بعجز الجميع ؛ جنهم وإنسهم ، مفترقين أو مجتمعين ، فقال : ﴿ قُل لَّبِنِ اجْتَمَعَتِ الإِنسُ وَالْجِنُّ عَلَى أَن يَأْتُوا بِمِثْلِ هَذَا الْقُرْءَانِ لَا يَأْتُونَ بِمِثْلِهِ، وَلَوْ كَانَ بَعْضُهُمْ لِبَعْضِ ظَهِيرًا ﴾ [الإسراء : ۸۸] ، ومع ذلك لم تتحرَّك أَنفَتُهم وهم المجبولونَ عليها ؟! ومِنْ عادتهم أنَّهم لا يتمالكونَ معَها ضبط أنفسهم عند ورودِ أدنى عارض يقدح في مناصبهم وإن كان في ذلك حتفُ أنفسهم ، فكيف بما هو مِنْ نوع البلاغة التي هي كلامهم وتَدِبُّ فيهم دبيباً ، حتى إنَّهم بها في كل وادٍ يهيمون ؟!
لكن القوم أخرسهم أنَّهم أحدُّوا أنَّ الأمر إلهي لا تمكنُ مقاومتُهُ ؛ إما لأنَّهُ ليسَ في طوقهم وهو الأصح ، أو للصَّرْفة ، وهما قولان
ومَنْ لم يستخي منهم ، وانْتَدَبَ لمقاومة هذا الأمر الإلهيّ ؛ كمُسَيْلِمَةَ . . افْتَضَحَ ، وأتى بمَخرَقةٍ يُتضاحَكُ منها إلى قيام الساعة
ولو أنَّهم نُقِلَ إليهمُ القرآنُ نقل غيرِهِ مِنَ الكلام نقل آحاد .. لأَمْكن الاعتذارُ عنهم بعدم الوصول ، كلا بل امتلاتْ بحَمَلَتِهِ وصُحُفِهِ وإشادة أمرِهِ الأَرضُ كلها ؛ سهلها بدوها وحضرها ، برها وبحرها، مؤمنُها وكافرها ، جِنُّها وإنسُها ، وتطاولتْ أزمنته على تلك الصفة قريباً مِنْ تسع مئة سنةٍ ، أفيستريب عاقل بعد هذا في كونهِ مِنْ عندِ اللهِ جَلَّ وعلا صدَّقَ بِهِ نبيَّه صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ ؟!
هذا معَ ما فيهِ مِنَ الإخبار قبل الوقوع بالغيوب المطابقة ، ومحاسنِ علوم الشريعة المشتملة على ما لا يَقدِرُ [؟]
Chapter
[ On the Statement of Establishing the Prophethood of Our Master Muhammad (peace be upon him) ]
Our Prophet and Master Muhammad (peace be upon him) - his claim to prophethood was known necessarily, and he challenged with miracles that cannot be encompassed.
[ The Miracle of the Mighty Quran ]
The greatest of them is the Mighty Quran, whose verses continually strike the ears of the eloquent [people] deluding every religion other than Islam, and it stirs, by requesting opposition in a way that incapacitates, the zeal of those sharp in intelligence, strong in eloquence in poetry and prose, those who plunge into every art of rhetoric length and breadth; such that no word, no matter how protected, escapes their opposition even if it does not allude to their inability. How [then] when they hear clear [؟] in their incapacitation the explicit saying of Him, the Exalted: "Then bring ten surahs like it, fabricated" [Hud:13], then He descended with them and said: "Then bring a surah from like it" [Baqara:23], then He declared the inability of all - their jinn and humans, separated or together - saying: "Say: 'If mankind and jinn gathered together to bring the like of this Quran, they would not bring its like, even if some of them were helpers to others'" [Isra:88]. Yet despite that their pride did not stir, while they were naturally disposed to it?! And it is their habit that they cannot control themselves with it when faced with the least disparagement of their status, even if that means their destruction. So how about what is of the type of eloquence which is their speech and permeates them, to the point that they wander in every valley through it?!
But the people were silenced because they realized that the matter is divine, not possible to resist; either because it is beyond their capability - and that is the more correct - or because of the sarfah [turning away], and these are two opinions.
And whoever among them did not shy away and stepped up to resist this divine command - like Musaylima - he was disgraced and came with a ruse that is laughed at until the Day of Judgment.
And if the Quran had been conveyed to them by single-narrator transmission like other speech, then an excuse for them [could] be possible due to non-arrival. But no! Rather, the whole earth filled with its carriers and its pages and the publicizing of its affair: its plains, its desert and its city, its land and its sea, its believer and its disbeliever, its jinn and its human, and its times lengthened in that manner for nearly nine hundred years. So can any rational person doubt after this that it is from Allah, the Mighty and Exalted, by which He confirmed His Prophet (peace be upon him)?!
This along with what it contains of news before occurrence of matching unseen matters, and the good qualities of the sciences of the Sharia which include what cannot be [؟].
Source pages p. 113

Commentary
This passage is a proof of the prophethood of Muhammad (peace be upon him) specifically through the miracle of the Quran. The author begins by stating that Muhammad's claim to prophethood is known necessarily (darurah) and that he challenged with countless miracles, the greatest being the Quran. Then he describes how the Quran continuously strikes the ears of eloquent Arabs, refuting all religions except Islam, and challenges them to produce something like it, thereby incapacitating their pride. He mentions three Quranic challenges: first, bring ten fabricated surahs like it (Hud:13); then, bring one surah like it (Baqara:23); finally, the absolute declaration that all humans and jinn combined cannot produce its like (Isra:88). Despite their extreme pride and sensitivity to any insult to their status, they did not respond to this challenge. The author points out that their silence proves the Quran is divine, beyond human power. He then presents two scholarly opinions on why they failed: (1) they were inherently incapable, which is the stronger view, or (2) Allah 'turned away' their ability (sarfah). He further illustrates that anyone who did attempt opposition, like Musaylima, was exposed and became a laughingstock. The author then argues that the Quran's transmission is not by isolated reports (ahad) but by mass transmission (tawatur) filling the whole earth, its carriers, pages, and renown spreading across all regions and times for nearly nine hundred years up to the author's era. Therefore, no rational person can deny that it is from Allah and a confirmation of Muhammad's prophethood. Finally, he adds internal evidence: the Quran contains accurate prophecies of future events and the comprehensive sciences of Sharia that no human can produce. The passage concludes with a broken sentence, but the argument is complete in essence.

Key Terms
التحدي
الإعجاز
الصرفة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Arabs failed to challenge the Quran because they were indifferent or lacked motivation.
Correction: The passage emphasizes their extreme pride and sensitivity, indicating their silence was due to genuine inability.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, what are the two opinions on why the Arabs failed to produce something like the Quran?
A) They were lazy, and they disliked the Prophet.
B) They were incapable, and Allah turned away their ability (sarfah).
C) They were not challenged properly, and the Quran was not widely known.
D) They considered it poetry, and they were busy with trade.

Key Takeaway
The Quran's inimitability, proven by the silent challenge, demonstrates its divine origin and validates Muhammad's prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the Quran’s challenge, do you feel a deep conviction that it is from Allah, or does your heart waver with doubts? What would it take for you to fully surrender to its authority today?
?
The Arabs’ pride blinded them from admitting the truth even when it was undeniable. Is there an area in your life—your career, relationships, or habits—where your own pride prevents you from submitting to a clear command of Allah? What step can you take this week to break that pride?
?
If the most eloquent Arabs stood silent before the Quran, what does that mean for your own attempts to justify disobedience or argue against its rulings? Will you let the Quran silence your excuses and change your heart, or will you cling to your own reasoning?

The Quran's Divine Origin: Transmission and Prophecies
Sanusi argues for the Quran's divine origin through tawatur and prophecies.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Quran's mass transmission and accurate prophecies establish it as a divine revelation confirming prophethood.

Core Idea
The Quran's uninterrupted widespread transmission and its fulfilled prophecies leave no room for doubt about its divine source.

After establishing the inimitability of the Quran, Sanusi presents further evidence: the Quran was transmitted through mass transmission (tawatur) across the globe, and it contains accurate prophecies of future events. This lesson explores these arguments that solidify the Quran's divine origin.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on Musaylima and transmission
Read from the example of Musaylima to the end. Notice how Sanusi contrasts the failed attempt of Musaylima with the widespread transmission of the Quran.
Musaylima is a historical figure who claimed prophethood and tried to produce similar 'revelations'.
2
Understand the argument from tawatur
Sanusi argues that the Quran was not transmitted by isolated reports but by continuous mass transmission, covering all regions and times for nearly nine centuries. Why does this eliminate excuses?
Tawatur means multiple independent chains of transmission that preclude collusion.
3
Consider the internal evidence of prophecies
The passage mentions that the Quran contains news of the unseen that came true and deep sciences of Sharia. Reflect on how this adds to its credibility.
The specific examples are not given here, but the principle is clear.

?

?

Additional Proofs of Prophethood
Sanusi lists additional proofs of the Prophet's prophethood beyond the Qur'an.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the multiple categories of evidence that confirm the Prophet's prophethood beyond the Qur'anic miracle.

Core Idea
Prophethood is confirmed by a convergence of miracles, perfections, scriptures, and divine providence.

The Qur'an is the greatest proof, but the Prophet's prophethood is further supported by an array of signs. This passage introduces three additional categories: his countless miracles, his perfect nature that almost spoke of his mission before it began, and the explicit mention of him in previous scriptures. A remarkable sign is that Allah prevented others from impersonating his name.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the translation. Notice the flow from miracles to perfections to scriptural confirmation to the divine protection of his name.
2
Identify the three categories of proofs
Sanusi lists three main categories: miracles (معجزات), perfections (كمالات), and scripture (الكتب الماضية). Under scripture, he includes a sub-proof about the name 'Muhammad'.
The perfections almost declared his prophethood before his mission.
3
Reflect on the name protection proof
Consider the striking detail that Allah prevented Arabs from bearing the name 'Muhammad' before him, except a few who hoped for prophethood. Yet none of them claimed prophethood. This removes any confusion.
This is presented as a divine grace removing doubt.
4
Connect to the broader argument
Ask yourself: Why does Sanusi add these proofs after the Qur'an? Because prophethood is established by multiple converging evidences, each reinforcing the other.
This shows the comprehensiveness of the proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[ قرائنُ أخرى على ثبوتِ نبوتِهِ عليه الصلاة والسلام ] ثم هذا إلى ما له من المعجزات التي لا تُحصى ، ثم إلى ما جُبِلَتْ عليه ذاتُهُ الكريمةُ من الكمالات التي كادت أن تُفصِحَ - بل أفصحَتْ - قبل مبعثِهِ برسالتِهِ خَلْقاً وخُلْقاً . ثم معَ ذلكَ كلِّهِ : أَكَّدَ الله تعالى صدْقَهُ بذكرِهِ باسمِهِ وبجميع وصفِهِ في الكتب الماضية ، قال تعالى : ﴿ الَّذِينَ يَتَّبِعُونَ الرَّسُولَ النَّبِيَّ الْأُمِّي ... ﴾ [الأعراف : ١٥٧] الآية . وأطلق السنة الأحبار قريباً من مبعثه بجميع ذلك . حتى إِنَّهُ سبحانَهُ بفضلِهِ مما أَكَدَ بهِ زوالَ اللَّبْسِ عن نبوّتِهِ أنْ منعَ العرب قبلَهُ من التسمي باسمِهِ الخاص بهِ ، إلا أُناساً قليلين تسموا قريباً من مولدِهِ باسمِهِ رجاءَ حصولِ النبوَّة لهم ؛ لما سمعوهُ من الأحبار ، ثم من عظيم فضل الله تعالى في إزالةِ اللَّبْسِ : أنْ لم يطلق لسان أحدٍ من أولئك الذينَ تسموا باسمه بدعوى النبوَّةِ .
[ Additional proofs of his prophethood, peace and blessings be upon him ] Then this, in addition to his countless miracles, and then to the perfections with which his noble essence was endowed – which almost declared – rather, they did declare – his mission before his sending, in creation and character. Then along with all that: Allah the Exalted confirmed his truth by mentioning him by his name and by all his attributes in the previous scriptures. He said the Exalted: {Those who follow the messenger, the unlettered prophet...} [Al-A'raf 7:157] – the verse. And the rabbis and scholars spoke near his time of all that. So much so that He, glorified be He, out of His grace, from what He established to remove doubt about his prophethood, is that He prevented the Arabs before him from being named with his specific name, except a few people who were named near his birth with his name hoping to attain prophethood, because they heard it from the scholars. Then from the great grace of Allah the Exalted in removing doubt: that He did not let the tongue of any of those who were named with his name make a claim to prophethood.
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage is a listing of additional proofs (قرائن) for the Prophet's prophethood. After establishing the Qur'anic miracle, the author presents three further categories: 1) his countless miracles, 2) his inherent perfections (both in creation and character) that almost explicitly indicated his prophethood even before his mission, 3) the confirmation in previous scriptures by name and attribute, citing the verse from al-A'raf. He then highlights a remarkable divine grace: Allah prevented Arabs before the Prophet from bearing his specific name (Muhammad), except a few who were named shortly before his birth in hope of prophethood, yet none of them ever claimed prophethood. This is presented as a powerful sign removing any possibility of confusion.

Correction: Sanusi shows multiple converging proofs: miracles, perfections, scriptures, and divine prevention of impersonation.

Prophethood is supported by a network of evidence including miracles, perfect character, scriptural predictions, and divine signs that prevent confusion.

Belief in the Unseen and Answering Objections
Sanusi states the obligation to believe in all unseen matters and answers an objection about the grave.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why belief in unseen matters like the punishment of the grave is obligatory despite apparent physical observations.

Core Idea
The grave's mysteries are miracles, not contradictions.

This passage concludes the proof of prophethood and extends it to all unseen matters. Sanusi addresses a natural doubt: how can we believe in punishment in the grave when we see the body unchanged? The answer lies in the principle of divine power over custom.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Let the author's flow come through before diving into commentary.
Note the examples of unseen matters and the objection.
2
Identify the examples and the objection
List the unseen matters mentioned (Gathering, Spreading, Path, Balance, etc.). Notice the objection: 'we see the dead as he was placed in his grave.'
3
Understand the answer: khawariq al-'adat
Sanusi explains that death and the grave involve violations of custom (khawariq al-'adat) which are possible. Since the Law informs about them, we must believe in their apparent meaning.
This upholds the principle that divine power can create states beyond normal experience.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإذا وُفِّقْتَ لعلم هذا كله حصلَ لكَ العلمُ ضرورةً بصدق رسالة نبينا ومولانا محمد صلى الله عليه وسلَّمَ فوجبَ الإيمانُ بهِ في كلِّ ما جاءَ بهِ عنِ الله سبحانه جملةً وتفصيلاً ; كالحشر والنشر ، والصراط والميزان ، والجنة والنار ، وعذاب القبر وسؤالِهِ . ولا يقدح فيه مشاهدتُنا للميت على نحو ما وُضِعَ في قبره ; لأنَّ في الموتِ وما بعده خوارق عاداتٍ أخبر بها الشرع، وهي جائزة، فوجب الإيمان بها على ظاهرها.
So if you are granted success in knowing all of this, necessary knowledge of the truth of the message of our Prophet and Master Muhammad, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, is attained, and thus faith in him becomes obligatory in everything he brought from Allah the Exalted, in general and in detail – such as the Gathering and the Spreading, the Path and the Balance, Paradise and the Fire, the punishment of the grave and its questioning. And our observation of the dead as he was placed in his grave does not detract from that; because in death and what follows it there are violations of custom which the Sacred Law has informed about, and they are possible, so belief in them according to their apparent meaning becomes obligatory.
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This passage is a conclusion and an objection-answer. It begins by stating that once one has attained necessary knowledge of the Prophet's truth through the previous proofs, one must have faith in everything he brought, both in general and in detail. The author lists examples of unseen matters: the Gathering, the Path, the Balance, Paradise, Hellfire, and the punishment and questioning in the grave. Then an objection is raised: we see the dead person in his grave as he was placed, so how can there be punishment or questioning? The answer: death and the grave involve miraculous occurrences (خوارق عادات) that are possible, and the Law has informed us of them, so we must believe in them in their apparent sense. This upholds the principle that divine power can create states beyond normal experience.

Misconception: Since the dead body appears unchanged in the grave, there is no punishment or questioning there.
Correction: The grave involves miraculous events (khawariq al-'adat) that are beyond normal perception but possible through divine power, as reported by the Law.

Key Takeaway
Belief in all unseen matters from the Prophet is obligatory; apparent physical evidence does not contradict because divine power can create exceptions to normal custom.

Textual Proofs for Exertion in Seeking Knowledge
Sanusi compiles hadiths, Quranic verses, and prophetic/salaf examples on effort in seeking knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scriptural evidence from hadith and Quran commanding effort and hardship in seeking knowledge, and the examples of the prophets and the righteous predecessors.

Core Idea
Knowledge requires exertion — prophets and righteous predecessors modeled it.

Sanusi brings together a series of textual proofs to demonstrate that seeking knowledge is not a passive endeavor. He cites hadiths, Quranic verses, and the examples of prophets and the salaf to show that effort, travel, and even weariness are part of the path. Let's examine each proof he marshals.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Let the various proofs flow together before breaking them down.
Notice the variety of sources: hadith, Quran, and historical examples.
2
Identify each proof
List each hadith, each Quranic verse, and each example Sanusi gives. See how many distinct proofs he provides.
There are three hadiths, two full Quranic verses, a partial verse, and two examples.
3
Reflect on the overall message
Ask: What is the common theme across all these proofs? How do they collectively emphasize the necessity of exertion?
The answer is that knowledge demands active seeking, travel, and hardship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد رُوِيَ في الحديث : ( لا يُستطاعُ العلم براحة الجسم (١) ، و أطْلُبُوا الْعِلْمَ وَلَوْ بِالصِّينِ (۲) ، وورد : « إِنَّمَا الْعِلْمُ بِالتَّعَلُّم (۳) وقال الله تعالى لنبيه يحيى عليهِ السلامُ : يَيَحْيَى خُذِ الْكِتَابَ بِقُوَّةٍ ﴾ [مريم : ۱۲] ، وقال لكليمه موسى عليهِ السلامُ : ﴿ وَكَتَبْنَا لَهُ فِي الْأَلْوَاحِ مِن كُلِّ شَيْءٍ .... إلى قولِهِ : ﴿ فَخُذْهَا بِقُوَّةٍ ﴾ [الأعراف : ١٤٥ ] ، وقال جل وعلا : ﴿فَلَوْلَا نَفَرَ مِن كُلِّ فِرْقَةٍ مِّنْهُمْ طَائِفَةٌ ... [التوبة : ١٢٢] الآية . وكانَ السلف الصالحُ يرتحلُ أحدهم لطلب الفائدة الواحدة مسير شهرٍ ، ولقد سافر كليم الله موسى عليهِ السلامُ مَعَ مَا أُعطِيَ مِنْ علمٍ كلٌّ شيء للقاء الخضر عليهِ السلامُ حتى مَسَّهُ التعب في ذلكَ ، وقال : لَقَدْ لَقِينَا مِن سَفَرِنَا هَذَا نَصَبا) [الكهف : ٦٢] (٤)
And it has been narrated in the hadith: 'Knowledge is not attained by bodily comfort' and 'Seek knowledge even if in China' and it is reported: 'Knowledge is only through learning.' And Allah the Exalted said to His prophet Yahya, peace be upon him: 'O Yahya, take the Book with strength' [Maryam 19:12]. And He said to His interlocutor Musa, peace be upon him: 'And We wrote for him on the tablets of everything... up to His saying: 'So take it with strength' [Al-A‘raf 7:145]. And He, Exalted and Glorious, said: 'So why did not a party from every group among them go forth...' [At-Tawba 9:122] the verse. And the righteous predecessors would travel for a month to seek a single benefit. And indeed the interlocutor of Allah, Musa, peace be upon him, despite the knowledge he was given of everything, traveled to meet Khidr, peace be upon him, until he experienced weariness from that, and said: 'We have indeed met from this journey of ours weariness' [Al-Kahf 18:62].
Source pages p. 150

Commentary
This passage is a collection of textual proofs (adilla naqliyya) supporting the obligation of effort in seeking knowledge. Sanusi cites three hadiths: 1) 'Knowledge is not attained by bodily comfort' (meaning one must work hard), 2) 'Seek knowledge even if in China' (emphasizing travel and perseverance), 3) 'Knowledge is only through learning' (i.e., it requires study). Then he cites Quranic commands: to Prophet Yahya to 'take the Book with strength' (i.e., with seriousness and exertion), and to Prophet Musa to 'take them (the tablets) with strength.' He also quotes the verse from Surah At-Tawba that encourages a group from each community to go forth to acquire religious knowledge. Finally, he gives the example of the righteous predecessors (salaf) who would travel long distances for a single benefit, and the story of Prophet Musa traveling to meet Khidr, despite his own great knowledge, enduring weariness. These examples reinforce that knowledge demands exertion, travel, and hardship, which is the opposite of passive taqlid.

Key Terms
الحديث (hadith)
السلف الصالح (al-salaf al-salih)
طلب العلم (talab al-‘ilm)
القوة (al-quwwa)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that seeking knowledge is easy or that one can attain it without effort.
Correction: This passage demonstrates that even prophets and the salaf endured hardship, and the Quran and hadith command exertion.

Key Takeaway
Sanusi shows through multiple sources that knowledge demands active seeking, effort, and even hardship — a duty for every seeker.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Refuting the Circularity Objection with a King's Analogy
Ibn al-Tilimsani answers the objection that proving God's speech by scripture is circular, using an analogy of a king.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ibn al-Tilimsani refutes the circularity objection using an analogy, showing that miracles directly indicate divine approval without requiring prior verbal testimony.

Core Idea
A miracle itself is God's direct affirmation of a prophet.

This lesson presents a powerful objection against proving God's speech (kalam nafsi) through scripture: that it would be circular because miracles already presuppose God's speech. Ibn al-Tilimsani responds with a vivid analogy that distinguishes between explicit verbal testimony and the signifying power of actions, particularly supernatural ones. This clarification protects the Ash'ari position from the charge of circular reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Objection's Logic
Read the objection carefully: scripture proves divine speech, but scripture depends on the prophet's truthfulness, which is established by a miracle, yet a miracle itself presupposes divine speech (as it is like God saying 'you are truthful'). Recognize the circularity.
The objection is strong; Ibn al-Tilimsani calls it 'a strong question'.
2
Follow the King-Prophet Analogy
Ibn al-Tilimsani presents an analogy: a claimant in the king's presence asks for a miracle as proof, and the king performs it. Everyone present knows the claimant is truthful without any verbal statement. See how the action alone suffices.
The king's action is the miracle, and it directly indicates the claimant's truthfulness.
3
Grasp How Miracles Function as Signs
The answer explains that miracles are like conventional signs or gestures that indicate God's will to affirm the prophet. They are not literal verbal testimony but are sufficient. The speech in dispute is inner speech (kalam nafsi), not created expressions.
This resolves the circularity because miracles do not require previous verbal speech.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل: يرد على إثبات كونه جل وعلا متكلماً بطريق السمع أن يقال: إن قول الرسول لا يدل ما لم يثبت صدقه، ولا يثبت صدقه إلا بالمعجزة، والمعجزة لا تثبت ما لم يثبت كون الباري تعالى متكلماً، فإن دلالة المعجزة تتنزل منزلة قول الله تعالى لمدعي الرسالة: صدقت، أو: أنت رسولي، فما لم يثبت الكلام [الصدق؟] لله تعالى لا يكون مصدقاً لرسله، فلو أثبتنا الكلام له تعالى بالسمع.. لدار. قلت: قال ابن التلمساني: (إنه سؤال قوي، وجوابه: أن من ادعى أنه رسول الملك بمرأى من الملك ومسمع، وقال: آية صدقي أن يغير الملك عادته المألوفة، ويفعل كذا، ثم قال: أيها الملك؛ إن كنت صادقاً في دعواي فافعل لي ذلك، ففعل ذلك على الوجه الذي التمسه.. فيعلم جميع الحاضرين أنه رسوله، وأنه صادق، وإن كان فيهم من ينفي كلام النفس، ويكفي في العلم بتصديقه إيجاده للفعل الدال على إرادة تصديقه كما يدل التخصيص في الأفعال على إرادة وقوعها على ذلك الوجه وقولهم: إن المعجزة تتنزل منزلة التصديق بالقول.. مسلم، ولكن تتنزل منزلة المواضعة على قول يدل على إرادة ذلك كما تدل بعض الإشارات على ذلك، والكلام المستدل على ثبوته لله تعالى بالسمع في دعوى الأشعرية هو القول النفسي، والنزاع فيه، لا في العبارات الحادثة المتواضع عليها، والأفعال كثيراً ما تدل على الإرادات وإن لم توضع لذلك، نظراً إلى العادات، والمعجزة كذلك ((1)).
If it is said: There is an objection to affirming that He, majestic and exalted, is mutakallim by way of scripture: that the statement of the messenger does not indicate anything unless his truthfulness is established, and his truthfulness is only established by a miracle, and the miracle is not established unless the existence of the Creator as mutakallim is established, for the indication of the miracle occupies the position of God's saying to the claimant of prophethood: 'You have spoken truth' or 'You are My messenger.' So as long as speech is not established, the truthfulness [؟] of God is not established to affirm his messengers. So if we establish speech for Him by scripture, a circularity occurs. I say: Ibn al-Tilimsani said: 'This is a strong question, and its answer is: Whoever claims that he is the messenger of a king in the king's sight and hearing, and says: The sign of my truthfulness is that the king changes his habitual practice and does such-and-such, then says: O king, if I am truthful in my claim, then do that for me, and he does it in the manner he requested. Then all those present know that he is his messenger and that he is truthful, even if among them are those who deny inner speech (kalam nafsi). And it suffices for knowing his affirmation that he brings about the act indicating the will to affirm him, just as specification in acts indicates the will for their occurrence in that manner. And their saying that the miracle occupies the position of verbal affirmation is granted, but it occupies the position of a conventional sign indicating the will for that, just as some gestures indicate that. And the speech whose existence for God is argued by scripture according to the Ash'ari claim is inner speech (al-qawl al-nafsi), and the dispute is about that, not about the created conventional expressions. And acts often indicate wills even if they are not conventionally placed for that, by consideration of habits, and the miracle is likewise.'
Source pages p. 291

Commentary
This is an objection-answer passage. The objection argues that proving God's speech by scripture is circular because scripture depends on the prophet's truthfulness, which is established by miracles, but miracles themselves presuppose God's speech (since they are God's testimony). Ibn al-Tilimsani answers with an analogy: a claimant to be a king's messenger in the king's presence asks for a miracle as proof; the king performs it, and all present know he is truthful without needing explicit verbal confirmation. Thus the miracle itself functions as a non-linguistic sign (like gesture or habitual act) indicating God's will to affirm the prophet. He also clarifies that the speech in question is inner speech (kalam nafsi), not created expressions, so the issue is not about literal verbal testimony.

Key Terms
معجزة
تصديق
كلام نفسي
عبارات حادثة
مواضعة
إرادة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Miracles require a prior verbal promise from God to be valid as proof of prophethood.
Correction: Ibn al-Tilimsani shows that a miracle itself is a direct sign of divine approval, no less effective than a verbal statement. The miracle occupies the position of a conventional sign indicating God's will, not a speech act.

Checkpoint
In Ibn al-Tilimsani's analogy, what does the king's action demonstrate?
A) That the king is a speaker.
B) That the claimant is truthful without needing a verbal statement.
C) That the miracle is the same as a verbal statement.
D) That the king does not need to speak.

Key Takeaway
Miracles are non-verbal but sufficient signs of divine approval, eliminating the need for explicit verbal testimony and thus avoiding circularity in proving God's speech.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever demanded a verbal sign from God when His actions already affirm His guidance in your life? What would it take for you to trust His silent endorsement through the patterns He has placed around you?
?
When you encounter a truth that is not spelled out in words but is unmistakably confirmed by circumstances, do you accept it or do you insist on a more explicit proof? How might this lesson challenge your reliance on verbal certainty over lived evidence?
?
Ibn al-Tilimsani shows that a king's action can declare a messenger without a word. What if God's signs in your own life are speaking louder than you are willing to hear? Are you waiting for a miracle you've already been given?

The Permissibility and Limits of Divine Knowledge
Sanusi enumerates four denied claims, argues for possibility of special knowledge, and questions certainty about others.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Sanusi's balanced position on special divine knowledge: its logical possibility, the specific claims he rejects, and the epistemological limits that prevent certainty about others' spiritual experiences.

Core Idea
Divine knowledge is possible but limited; claims of surpassing prophethood or encompassing God are rejected.

Sanusi walks a careful line between affirming God's power to grant special knowledge and rejecting exaggerated claims that undermine prophethood. In this passage, he clarifies what he denies, argues for the rational possibility of deeper perception, and then humbly admits the limits of what we can know about others' states. This lesson unpacks his reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify denials and allowances
Read the passage and note what Sanusi explicitly denies vs. what he allows. He first says he does not deny that Allah may grant special knowledge, then lists four specific claims he rejects.
The four claims are: immediate vision, advancement over prophethood, participation in prophethood, and encompassing knowledge.
2
Understand the argument for possibility
Sanusi uses an analogy with the afterlife: if God can create a more perfect perception of Himself in the Hereafter, then the intellect cannot deem it impossible for Him to create a similar perception in the heart now.
This argument establishes the logical possibility, not actual occurrence.
3
Consider epistemological limits
Sanusi notes that such matters are subjective (wijdān) and that he only knows his own state. He cannot know others' states without a truthful report, which has not been established.
He also questions whether Sufi claims pertain to the Essence or to deeper knowledge of attributes.
4
Reflect on the final verse
The passage ends with the Prophet's prayer for increase in knowledge (Quran 20:114), implying that even the most knowledgeable should seek more, leaving room for further divine gifts.
This reinforces the open-ended nature of divine knowledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَنَحْنُ لَا نُنْكِرُ أَنْ يَخُصَّ اللهُ تَعَالَى عَبْداً مِنْ عَبِيدِهِ بِعِلْمٍ مَا، كَمَا قَالَ تَعَالَى فِي الْخَضِرِ: ﴿وَعَلَّمْنَاهُ مِن لَّدُنَّا عِلْماً﴾ [الكهف: 65]، وَإِنَّمَا نُنْكِرُ عَلَى مَنْ يَدَّعِي رُؤْيَةً عَاجِلَةً، أَوْ تَقَدُّماً عَلَى دَرَجَةِ النُّبُوَّةِ، أَوْ مُشَارَكَةً فِيهَا، أَوْ أَنَّهُ عَالِمٌ بِاللهِ تَعَالَى عِلْمَ إِحَاطَةٍ. وَإِذَا جَازَ خَلْقُ إِدْرَاكٍ لَنَا بِاللهِ تَعَالَى فِي الْآخِرَةِ هُوَ أَتَمُّ إِدْرَاكاً مِنْ إِدْرَاكِنَا الَّذِي هُوَ مَعْرِفَةُ الْمُؤَثِّرِ بِأَثَرِهِ .. فَلَا يَجْزِمُ الْعَقْلُ بِاسْتِحَالَةِ خَلْقِ مِثْلِ ذَلِكَ فِي الْقَلْبِ، وَيَكُونُ نِسْبَةُ مَا تَعَلَّقَ بِهِ فِي الْوُضُوحِ وَالْجَلَاءِ كَنِسْبَةِ الْحَاصِلِ عَنِ الرُّؤْيَةِ. فَالْحَقُّ إِذاً: أَنْ نَجْزِمَ بِجَوَازِ ذَلِكَ، وَلَا اسْتِحَالَةَ، وَإِذَا كَانَ ذَلِكَ يَرْجِعُ إِلَى الْوِجْدَانِ - وَفَضْلُ اللهِ تَعَالَى لَا نِهَايَةَ لَهُ - فَلَا عِلْمَ لِي إِلَّا بِحَالِ نَفْسِي، وَحَالُ غَيْرِي لَا أَعْرِفُهُ إِلَّا بِإِنْبَاءٍ صَادِقٍ فِي الْعَادَةِ، وَلَمْ يُوجَدْ، وَمَا يَدَّعِيهِ الصُّوفِيَّةُ لَمْ نُمَيِّزْهُ فَنَعْلَمُ أَنَّ ذَلِكَ الْمُدْرَكَ يَرْجِعُ إِلَى الذَّاتِ مِنْ وَجْهٍ أَوْ إِلَى تَرَقٍّ فِي الْعِلْمِ بِالصِّفَاتِ وَالْأَسْمَاءِ .. فَكَيْفَ لَنَا بِالْجَزْمِ أَنَّ اللهَ تَعَالَى لَمْ يَخْلُقْ لِصِدِّيقٍ وَلَا نَبِيٍّ مُرْسَلٍ سِوَى مَا نَعْلَمُهُ نَحْنُ مِنَ اللهِ تَعَالَى؟! وَاللهُ عَزَّ وَجَلَّ يَقُولُ لِأَعْلَمِ الْخَلْقِ: ﴿وَقُل رَّبِّ زِدْنِي﴾ [طه: 114]
And we do not deny that Allah the Exalted may specify a servant from among His servants with some knowledge, as He said the Exalted concerning al-Khiḍr: 'And We taught him from Our presence a knowledge' [al-Kahf: 65]. But we only deny against one who claims an immediate vision (ruʾyah ʿājilah), or advancement over the rank of prophethood, or participation in it, or that he is a knower of Allah the Exalted with encompassing knowledge (ʿilm iḥāṭah). And if it is permissible for Allah to create a perception (idrāk) of Him in the Hereafter that is more complete in perception than our perception which is the knowledge of the effect from its cause... then the intellect cannot affirm the impossibility of creating something like that in the heart, and the proportion of what is grasped thereby in clarity and manifestation would be like the proportion of what results from vision. So the truth is: that we affirm the permissibility of that, and no impossibility. And if that returns to personal experience (al-wijdān) - and the favor of Allah the Exalted is without end - then I have no knowledge except of my own state, and the state of others I do not know except by a truthful report (inbāʾ ṣādiq) that is customary, and it has not been found. And what the Sufis claim we have not distinguished, so that we know whether that perceived thing pertains to the Essence (al-dhāt) in some respect or to an elevation in knowledge of the attributes (ṣifāt) and names (asmāʾ)... So how for us to have certainty that Allah the Exalted did not create for any saint (ṣiddīq) nor sent prophet except what we ourselves know of Allah the Exalted?! And Allah, Almighty and Majestic, says to the most knowledgeable of creation: 'And say: My Lord, increase me' [Ṭā Hā: 114].
Source pages p. 343

Commentary
This passage discusses the scope and limits of special divine knowledge. The author first states that he does not deny that God can grant specific knowledge to a servant, as He taught al-Khiḍr (Quran 18:65). However, he objects to four specific claims: (1) claiming an immediate vision of God (ruʾyah ʿājilah) in this life, (2) claiming advancement over the rank of prophethood, (3) claiming participation in prophethood itself, and (4) claiming encompassing knowledge (ʿilm iḥāṭah) of God. 

The author then presents an argument for the possibility of such perception: Since God will create a perception of Himself in the afterlife that is more complete than our current knowledge (which is merely knowing the effect from its cause), the intellect cannot deem it impossible for God to create a similar perception in the heart in this world. The clarity of that perception would be comparable to actual vision. Therefore, the correct position is to affirm the logical possibility of such perception.

He then shifts to epistemological limits: such matters are subjective (wijdān), and God's favor is infinite. The author admits he only knows his own state; he can only know the state of others by truthful customary report (inbāʾ ṣādiq fī al-ʿādah), which has not been established. Regarding the Sufis' claims, he says they have not been distinguished enough to know whether the perceived object relates to God's Essence (al-dhāt) or to a deeper understanding of His attributes and names. The author questions how we can be certain that God did not bestow some knowledge on any saint or prophet beyond what we ourselves know. He ends by quoting the Prophet's prayer for increase in knowledge (Quran 20:114), implying that even the most knowledgeable should seek more. This demonstrates a balanced approach: affirming the possibility while rejecting unverified claims.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Denying claims like immediate vision or surpassing prophethood means denying that God can grant any special knowledge.
Correction: Sanusi explicitly affirms that God can grant special knowledge, as He did with al-Khiḍr, and argues for its possibility; he only denies specific exaggerated claims.

Checkpoint
Which of the following claims does the author explicitly deny?
A) That God can grant special knowledge to a servant
B) The claim of immediate vision or advancement over prophethood
C) That the intellect can affirm impossibility of divine perception
D) That the Sufis have no knowledge

Key Takeaway
Sanusi affirms the logical possibility of special divine knowledge while firmly rejecting any claim that implies surpassing or encompassing the rank of prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When was the last time you claimed to have a special insight from God that you could not verify through scripture or reason? How does Sanusi's admission that he only knows his own state confront that claim?
?
You often judge others' spiritual experiences as either authentic or deluded. But Sanusi insists he cannot know the state of others without a truthful report. Will you now hesitate before dismissing or exalting someone's claimed encounter with God? What would it take for you to seek that truthful report first?
?
The Prophet ﷺ was commanded to pray 'My Lord, increase me in knowledge.' When did you last genuinely pray that prayer with your heart? What holds you back from begging Allah for more knowledge of Him, even while you may feel satisfied with what you already know?

Moses' Overwhelming Experience of Divine Speech
Narrates Moses' condition after hearing divine speech and the wonder of his survival.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Moses' encounter with God's eternal speech transformed his perception of creation and how only God's sustaining power preserved him from annihilation.

Core Idea
Hearing God's speech can overwhelm a prophet, yet God's mercy preserves him.

This lesson explores a remarkable narrated event in the life of Prophet Moses after he received direct speech from Allah. The passage describes how the intensity of that divine encounter made the sounds of ordinary creation unbearable to him, and how only Allah's grace kept him intact. As we read, reflect on the overwhelming majesty of God's speech and the profound effect it had on a chosen prophet.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Let the narrative flow before analyzing details.
Notice the dramatic contrasts: divine pleasure vs. repugnant sounds.
2
Identify Moses' reaction
What did Moses do upon returning from the mountain? Why did he cover his ears? The passage says created sounds became like 'repugnant beasts.'
3
Consider the role of divine veiling
The passage states that if Allah had not veiled Moses from what he tasted, he would never feel at ease with creation. Why would that be?
This shows the intense pleasure of divine speech.
4
Reflect on the marvel of preservation
The most amazing part is that Moses' self did not dissolve. What kept him from annihilation? How does this relate to Allah's power over the heavens and earth?
This highlights both the majesty of God and His mercy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ورُوِيَ : أنَّ موسى عليهِ السلامُ عند قدومِهِ مِنَ المناجاة كانَ يسدُّ أذنيه لئلا يسمعَ كلامَ الخلْقِ) ؛ إذْ صارَ عندَهُ كأَشدَّ ما يكونُ مِنْ أصوات البهائم المنكرةِ ، حتى لم يكن يستطيع سماعه ؛ بحِدْثانِ ما ذاقَ مِنَ اللذَّاتِ التي لا يُحاط بها ولا تُكيَّفُ . . عند سماع كلامٍ مَنْ ليس كمثلِهِ شيءٌ جلَّ وعلا ، ولولا أنه سبحانَهُ يغيّبُهُ عمَّا ذاقَ عندَ مناجاتِهِ ممَّا لا يُقدَرُ على وصفِهِ.. لَمَا أمكن أنْ يأنس إلى شيءٍ مِنَ المخلوقات أبداً ، ولَما انتفعَ ِبهِ أحدٌ ، فسبحانَهُ مِنْ لطيف ما أوسعَ كرمَهُ وأعظم جلاله ! ومن أعجب الأمورِ في هذا : عدم ذوبان الذاتِ مِنْ موسى عليهِ الصلاة والسلام وتلاشيها حتى تصير عدماً محضاً ؛ عندَ اطِّلاعِها مِنْ ذي الجلال على ما اطَّلَعَتْ ، لولا أنَّهُ ثَبَّتَها وأمسكها الذي أمسكَ السماوات والأرض .
And it is narrated that Moses, peace be upon him, upon his return from the private meeting (munājāh) used to plug his ears so as not to hear the speech of creatures, for it became to him like the most severe of repugnant sounds of beasts, so that he could not bear to hear it, due to the freshness of what he had tasted of pleasures that cannot be encompassed nor qualified... upon hearing the speech of the One of whom nothing is like Him, majestic and exalted. And were it not that He, glorified is He, veils him from what he tasted during his private meeting, which cannot be described... it would never be possible for him to feel at ease with any creature ever, nor would anyone benefit from him. So glorified is He, how vast is His kindness and how great is His majesty! And among the most amazing things in this is the non-dissolution of the self of Moses—peace and blessings be upon him—and its annihilation until it becomes pure non-existence, upon its beholding from the Possessor of Majesty what it beheld, were it not that He made it firm and held it, the One who holds the heavens and the earth.
Source pages p. 380

Commentary
This passage describes the profound effect on Moses after he heard God's speech. Upon returning from the mountain, he covered his ears because the sounds of creatures seemed unbearable compared to the pleasure of hearing God's eternal speech. The author notes that if God did not veil Moses from that experience, he would never be able to interact with creation again. Then the author marvels that Moses' self did not dissolve and become nothing when it was exposed to such divine manifestation; only God's sustaining power kept him intact. This highlights the overwhelming majesty of God's speech and the grace of God in preserving Moses.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Moses heard God's speech as ordinary audible sound without any transformative effect.
Correction: The passage shows that hearing God's eternal speech caused Moses to perceive all creation's sounds as repugnant, indicating a profound, overwhelming experience beyond ordinary hearing.

Checkpoint

A) He was in pain
B) Created sounds seemed repugnant after hearing God's speech
C) He wanted to be alone
D) He was commanded to do so

Key Takeaway
The experience of divine speech can overwhelm a prophet's senses, yet Allah's mercy preserves them from annihilation and enables them to continue their mission.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The passage says that were it not for Allah veiling Moses from the intensity of that experience, he could never feel at ease with any creature. What does this suggest about the nature of divine encounters? Are you seeking such encounters, and are you prepared for how they might change your perception of everything else?
?
Can you honestly say that you have ever experienced even a fraction of the pleasure of divine remembrance that Moses tasted? If not, what is holding you back from seeking it more earnestly? What one change will you make today to prioritize seeking closeness to Allah over worldly sounds?

The Necessity of Tawhid for Validating Prophethood
Sanusi refutes the claim that knowledge of prophethood is independent of knowing divine unity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why knowledge of prophethood logically depends on prior knowledge of divine unity, refuting the view of Abu Hashim.

Core Idea
A miracle proves the prophet only if we know God alone can perform it.

Sanusi addresses a subtle but critical claim: that prophethood can be known independently of knowing God's oneness. He shows that unless we already know that only God can produce a true miracle, the miracle itself cannot confirm the prophet's truthfulness. This passage clarifies the logical priority of tawhid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim
Read the first part describing Abu Hashim's view that prophethood leads to knowledge of tawhid.
Notice that Abu Hashim thinks prophethood can be known without prior tawhid.
2
Understand the objection
Sanusi does not accept this independence. He argues that we must first know God's exclusivity.
3
Follow the reasoning
Trace why a miracle's evidential value requires prior knowledge that only God can perform such acts.
The miracle functions as God's endorsement, like saying 'You are truthful.'
4
Connect to kalam foundations
Realize that this argument shows tawhid as the foundational truth from which all other theological knowledge flows.
Prophethood is not independent; it rests on tawhid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإذا أظهر الرسولُ معجزةً على أنَّهُ رسولُهُ ، وأثبت صدقَهُ بتصديقِهِ لهُ .. فقد ثبت صدقُهُ ، فإذا أخبرَ بأَنْ لا إلهَ غيرُه ، ولا خالق سواه .. فقد ثبتَتِ الوحدانية ، وهذه المقالة تنقل عن أبي هاشم . ويَرِدُ عليها : أنَّنا لا نُسلّمُ أنَّ العلم بصحة النبوَّةِ لا يتوقَّفُ على ذلكَ ، وبيانُه : أَنَّ القائل بأنَّهُ رسولُ إذا ادَّعى الرسالة ، وأقام الخارق على صدقه .. فلا يدلُّ وجود الخارقِ على صدقِهِ ما لم يُتحقَّق أنَّ هذا الفعلَ الذي جاءَ بهِ لا يقدر عليهِ غيرُ مُرسِلهِ ؛ ليكونَ فعله مطابقاً لتحدّيهِ ، وسؤاله نازلاً منزلة قولِهِ : صدقت ، فإذا لم يكن لنا علم بنفي فاعليَّةِ غيرِه .. فلا يُعلَمُ أَنَّهُ فعلُهُ ، ولا يتم ذلك إلا بعد إثباتِ أَنَّ هذا الخارق - كإحياء الموتى مثلاً - لا يفعله غيرُ اللَّهِ عزَّ وجلَّ ، وذلكَ يتوقَّفُ على إثباتِ الوحدانية
When the prophet shows a miracle indicating that he is His messenger, and he establishes his truthfulness by His confirming him... then his truthfulness is established. Then when he informs that there is no god but Him, and no creator other than Him... then divine unity is established. This statement is transmitted from Abu Hashim. An objection is raised against it: that we do not concede that knowledge of the validity of prophethood does not depend on that. Its explanation: that the one who says that he is a messenger, when he claims prophethood and produces a supernatural event (al-khariq) as proof of his truthfulness... the existence of the supernatural event does not indicate his truthfulness unless it is verified that this act which he brought cannot be done by anyone other than his sender; so that his act matches his challenge, and his request takes the place of his saying: 'You have spoken truthfully.' So if we have no knowledge negating the agency of another... then it is not known that it is His act. And that is not completed except after establishing that this supernatural event—like reviving the dead, for example—is not done by anyone other than Allah, Exalted and Majestic. And that depends on establishing divine unity (al-wahdaniyya).
Source pages p. 431

Commentary
This passage presents an objection to the view attributed to Abu Hashim that one can know the truthfulness of a prophet and thereby know divine unity without prior knowledge of God's oneness. The author first states the view: when a prophet shows a miracle, his truthfulness is proven, and then when he announces that there is no god but God, divine unity is proven. The objection is then raised: we do not concede that knowledge of prophethood is independent of divine unity. The explanation follows: for a miracle (al-khariq) to prove the prophet's truthfulness, we must be certain that the act is beyond the power of any agent other than the one who sent him. This is because the miracle functions as a verbal confirmation: the prophet's request for a miracle is like saying 'I am truthful,' and God's performing it is like saying 'You are truthful.' But if we do not know that no other agent can perform it, we cannot attribute it to God. Therefore, establishing that the miracle is solely God's act requires first establishing that God is one and unique in His power (al-wahdaniyya). Thus, knowledge of prophethood depends on prior knowledge of tawhid.

Key Terms
الخارق (al-khariq)
الوحدانية (al-wahdaniyya)
صدق الرسول
معجزة
أبو هاشم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that miracles alone suffice to prove prophethood without prior knowledge of God's oneness.
Correction: Miracles only indicate truthfulness if we already know that only God can perform them, which requires prior knowledge of tawhid.

Checkpoint
According to the objection in this passage, why does a miracle not prove a prophet's truthfulness unless divine unity is established?
A) Because the prophet might be a magician.
B) Because the miracle must be known to be exclusively from God.
C) Because the miracle must be witnessed by many.
D) Because the prophet must first prove his own existence.

Key Takeaway
Knowledge of prophethood is inseparable from and dependent on knowledge of God's oneness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Before studying this lesson, did you assume that miracles alone prove a prophet? How does your certainty about prophethood now rest on your conviction that God alone is the Creator?
?
If you were challenged to prove that only Allah can bring a dead person back to life, could you do it from your belief in tawhid? What aspect of God's unity gives you that confidence?
?
Have you ever affirmed prophethood without fully grasping that it depends on tawhid? What changes in your heart when you realize that your faith in prophets is built on the foundation of God's oneness?

Prophethood Requires Tawhid
Sanusi concludes that establishing a divine sender is impossible without knowing God's oneness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the establishment of prophethood rationally depends on knowledge of God's oneness (tawhid).

Core Idea
Without tawhid, no miracle can be attributed to a divine sender.

Sanusi concludes his argument by showing that even the proof of prophethood—through miracles—requires prior knowledge of tawhid. In this passage, he explains why identifying the agent of a miracle is impossible if we do not already know that God is one. This deepens our understanding of the logical priority of tawhid over all other theological truths.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Sanusi references his own work, al-‘Aqida, as support.
2
Identify the core claim
Find the statement: 'the establishment of the Maker for a specific action is not realized without divine unity.' This is the central thesis.
This claim directly links tawhid to knowledge of God's actions.
3
Trace the logical chain
Follow the argument: without tawhid, you cannot attribute any action to a specific agent; miracles are actions; therefore you cannot attribute a miracle to God as sender.
The chain has four clear steps: (1) no tawhid → (2) agent of any action unknown → (3) miracle is an action → (4) sender of miracle unknown.
4
Relate to the broader lesson
Consider why this conclusion is placed at the end of the discussion on the verse. It reinforces that rational proof for tawhid is necessary before prophethood can be established.
5
Reflect on the implication
If prophethood depends on tawhid, then the study of tawhid must come first. This is a foundational principle in Islamic theology.
This connects to the overall structure of the creed.

فأنت ترى كيف مالَ إلى عدم الاكتفاء بالسمع في معرفة الوحدانية بما أوردَهُ مِنَ الحُجَّةِ على ذلكَ ، وإلى قريب منها أشرتُ في العقيدة بقولي : ( لأنَّ ثبوت الصانع لا يتحقق بدونِها ... ) إلى آخره ؛ يعني : أنَّ ثبوت الصانع على سبيل التعيين لفعل مِنَ الأفعال لا يَتحقَّقُ بدون الوحدانية ؛ إذ على تقدير عدمِها لا يُدرى في كلِّ فعلٍ مَنْ فعلَهُ ، ومِنْ جملة ذلكَ : الخارقُ الذي ظهر على يد الرسولِ؛ فإِنَّهُ لا يُدرى على تقدير عدمِ معرفةِ الوحدانيةِ مَنِ المُرْسِلُ الذي خلق ذلكَ الخارق على يد الرسولِ ليصدَّقَهُ بهِ ، فصارَ ثبوت الصانع المرسل مجهولاً
So you see how he inclined to not being satisfied with revelation (al-sam‘) in knowing divine unity, by what he presented of the proof for that. And near to that I indicated in al-‘Aqida by my saying: 'Because the establishment of the Maker is not realized without it...' to the end of it. Meaning: that the establishment of the Maker specifically for an action is not realized without divine unity; because if it were absent, it would not be known in every action who did it. And among that is the miraculous event (al-khariq) that appeared at the hand of the messenger; for indeed, it would not be known, given the absence of knowledge of divine unity, who is the sender who created that miracle at the hand of the messenger to confirm him by it. So the establishment of the sending Maker becomes unknown.
Source pages p. 432

Commentary
This passage is the author's concluding remark reinforcing the earlier argument. He observes that the previous discussion (referring to the objection and verse analysis) shows a tendency to not rely solely on revelation (al-sam‘) for knowledge of tawhid; rather, rational proof is needed. The author then references his own work (al-‘Aqida) where he said that establishing the Maker (al-Sani‘) is not realized without tawhid. He explains: to know that a specific act is from God—like the miracle performed through a prophet—we must first know that God is one and unique. Without tawhid, we cannot identify the agent behind any act, including the miracle. Thus, the identity of the sender (the one who creates the miracle) remains unknown, meaning prophethood itself becomes unknowable. Therefore, tawhid is logically prior to prophethood.

الوحدانية
الصانع (al-Sani‘)

Misconception: Prophethood can be proved without first establishing tawhid.
Correction: The author shows that identifying the sender of a miracle—the central proof of prophethood—requires prior knowledge that God is one and the only agent.

Checkpoint
Why does the author say that without divine unity, the establishment of the sending Maker becomes unknown?
A) Because God's attributes cannot be known.
B) Because we cannot attribute a specific miracle to God without knowing He is the only agent.
C) Because prophethood is proved by reason alone.
D) Because the prophet might be lying.

Key Takeaway
Without tawhid, we cannot attribute any event—including miracles—to God, making prophethood rationally unknowable.

Consider a time you struggled to see God's hand in an event. Was that struggle rooted in a lack of firm belief in tawhid? What concrete step will you take today to strengthen your conviction that all actions, big and small, are from God alone?

Objection and Answer: Miracle Proves Both Truthfulness and Tawhid
Objection that miracle proves both tawhid and truthfulness; answer distinguishes types of circularity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the objection that a miracle can prove both tawhid and truthfulness without circularity is answered by distinguishing between two types of circularity: priority and simultaneity.

Core Idea
Not all circles are vicious; a simultaneous circle of proof can be valid.

This passage presents a sophisticated objection to the earlier proof of prophethood. The objector argues that if a miracle can indicate both the prophet's truthfulness and the truth of tawhid at the same time, then no separate proof for tawhid is needed. The response clarifies that the resulting circularity is one of simultaneity, not priority, and is therefore logically permissible. Let's follow the argument carefully.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and response
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the structure: the objector makes a case, then two possible answers are given.
The passage uses technical terms like 'dawr ma'iyya'.
2
Identify the two responses
The author presents two distinct rejoinders. The first appeals to the rational nature of the miracle's indication. The second concedes the dependence on tawhid but argues for simultaneous proof.
3
Understand the key distinction
The crucial point is the difference between 'dawr taqaddum' (circle of priority) and 'dawr ma'iyya' (circle of simultaneity). Only the former is impossible in demonstration.
This distinction is essential for the defense.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد اعترض بعضُ المعاصرين في شرح له على العقيدة المنسوبة لابن الحاجب هذهِ الحُجَّةَ التي اعتمدها شرفُ الدين بن التلمساني ، وأشرنا إليها في عقيدتنا . . بما نصه بعد حكاية إيرادِ شرف الدين : ( قد يُقالُ في جوابِهِ : إِنَّ دلالة الخارقِ على صِدْقِ مَنْ تَحدَّى بِهِ عقليَّةٌ على أحد القولين ، وإذا كانَتْ عقليَّةً فلا يصح تخلُّفُ المدلول عنها ، وإلا انقلب الدليل شبهةً . أو نقولُ : سلَّمْنا توقُفَهُ على ثبوتِ الوحدانية ، للكنْ لِمَ لا يكونُ ظهورُ الخارقِ دليلاً على الصدْقِ وعلى ثبوتِ الوحدانية معاً ؟! فالدورُ اللازم غيرُ ممتنع لأنَّه دورُ معيَّة ، والبرهانُ إنَّما قام على استحالة التقدم ) انتهى
And a contemporary scholar objected in his commentary on the creed attributed to Ibn al-Hajib to this argument that Sharaf al-Din ibn al-Tilmisani adopted, and we referred to it in our creed, with his text after narrating Sharaf al-Din's objection: 'It may be said in response to him: The indication of the miracle (al-khāriq) to the truthfulness of the one who challenges with it is rational (ʿaqliyya) according to one of the two opinions. And if it is rational, then the indicated cannot fail to follow, otherwise the proof would turn into a fallacy. Or we say: We grant that it depends on the establishment of divine unity, but why should the appearance of the miracle not be evidence for truthfulness and for the establishment of divine unity together? So the required circularity (al-dawr al-lāzim) is not impossible because it is circularity of simultaneity (dawr maʿiyya), and the demonstration (al-burhān) only established the impossibility of priority (al-taqaddum).' End.
Source pages p. 433

Commentary
This passage presents an objection and a response to the earlier argument that knowledge of tawhid is necessary before a miracle can prove prophethood. The objector is a contemporary commentator on Ibn al-Hajib's creed. He raises two possible rejoinders. First, he says that according to one opinion, the miracle's indication of the challenger's truthfulness is rational (as opposed to conventional or prescriptive). If it is rational, then the conclusion (the challenger's truthfulness) must follow necessarily; otherwise the proof becomes a mere fallacy. Second, he concedes that the miracle's proof of truthfulness may depend on knowing tawhid, but he asks: why cannot the miracle itself prove both truthfulness and tawhid simultaneously? The resulting circularity would be a 'circle of simultaneity' (dawr maʿiyya), not a circle of priority (dawr taqaddum). The impossibility of circularity in demonstration applies only to priority circles (where A is prior to B and B prior to A in the same respect). A simultaneity circle, where two things are mutually dependent and known together, is not logically impossible. Thus the objection is answered: the miracle can indeed serve as evidence for both tawhid and the prophet's truthfulness at once, without falling into the impossible circularity that the author warned against.

Key Terms
خارق
دور معية
دور تقدم
عقلية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All circular reasoning is invalid in theological proofs.
Correction: Only circularity of priority (dawr taqaddum) is invalid; circularity of simultaneity (dawr ma'iyya) is permissible when two truths are mutually confirming.

Checkpoint
According to the objector's response, why is the circularity from a miracle proving both tawhid and truthfulness not impossible?
A) Because the miracle is a rational proof that cannot fail.
B) Because it is a circle of simultaneity, not of priority.
C) Because the objector rejects the need for tawhid entirely.
D) Because the proof of the miracle is conventional.

Key Takeaway
A simultaneous circle (dawr ma'iyya) is not a logical fallacy; thus a miracle can be evidence for both the prophet's truthfulness and the oneness of Allah at the same time.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever dismissed a truth because it seemed circular without examining the type of circle? This lesson shows that some circles are permissible. Is there a belief you've rejected due to superficial circularity that you should reconsider? What would it take for you to re-examine it honestly?
?
The miracle of the Quran is meant to prove both tawhid and prophethood simultaneously. Do you approach the Quran with that integrated conviction, or do you treat tawhid and prophethood as separate proofs in your heart? Which one do you lean on more, and why?
?
If a simultaneous circle is valid, what might be some other truths in your faith that validate each other mutually rather than in a chain? How does that change the way you explain your beliefs to someone skeptical of linear proofs?
