The Qur'an's Agreement with Reason: Acknowledged but Not the Challenge
Sanusi acknowledges the rational agreement but denies it as the basis of the challenge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Sanusi's position that while the Qur'an agrees with rational principles, this agreement was not the basis of the miraculous challenge.

Core Idea
Rational agreement is a quality of the Qur'an, not the challenge.

In this passage, Sanusi addresses a specific theory about the Qur'an's miraculousness: that it lies in its conformity to rational judgments. He acknowledges this quality but firmly distinguishes it from the actual challenge (tahaddi) that proves i'jaz. This distinction is crucial for understanding what makes the Qur'an inimitable.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation once. Notice the structure: 'As for the one who says... we do not deny... but the challenge was not made with that.' This is a concession followed by a qualification.
2
Identify the two parts: acknowledgment and denial
Sanusi agrees that agreement with reason is a description of the Qur'an, but he denies that this was the basis of the challenge. Understand why he makes this distinction.
3
Reflect on the implication
Ask yourself: if rational agreement were the challenge, could other rational texts claim the same? The specific challenge was about linguistic inimitability, not general rationality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأَمَّا مَنْ قالَ : إعجازه بموافقتِهِ لقضايا العقول : فلا ننكر أيضاً أنَّ ذلكَ وصفه، لَكنَّ التحدي لم يقع بذلك
As for the one who says: its miraculousness is its agreement with the judgments of the intellects: we also do not deny that that is its description, but the challenge was not made with that.
Source pages p. 585

Commentary
This passage addresses the view that the Qur'an's miraculousness is its conformity to rational principles (muwafaqatuhu li qadaya al-'uqul). The author does not deny that the Qur'an indeed conforms to sound reason – that is a correct description. However, he again points out that the challenge (tahaddi) was not made on this basis. The reason, by implication, is that rational agreement is a general quality that could be claimed for many texts, and the specific challenge was about linguistic and stylistic inimitability. Thus, while the Qur'an is rational, that is not the specific miracle of the challenge.

Key Terms
موافقة
قضايا العقول

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that the Qur'an's agreement with reason is the basis of its inimitability.
Correction: Sanusi clarifies that while it is a description, the actual challenge was not made on that basis.

Checkpoint
What is the author's position on the view that i'jaz is the Qur'an's agreement with reason?
A) He denies it completely
B) He accepts it as the basis of the challenge
C) He agrees it is a description but says the challenge was not made with it
D) He says it is a weak argument

Key Takeaway
Sanusi affirms the Qur'an's rationality but insists that the miraculous challenge was not based on that.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever treated the Qur'an as merely a rational book, forgetting that its true power lies in its unique, inimitable challenge? How does that change your approach to reading it starting today?
?
The author acknowledges that the Qur'an agrees with reason, but denies that this is the basis of its miracle. If you are only convinced by rational arguments for Islam, are you missing the deeper call of the Qur'an? What will you do to respond to that call?
?
If the challenge of the Qur'an is not simply its reasonableness but something that demands a response, what is that response you have been withholding? Commit today to one specific action that acknowledges the Qur'an's unique authority over you.

The Chosen Miracle: Eloquence and the Challenge of a Surah
Sanusi announces the settled conclusion on the basis of i'jaz and the form of the challenge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Sanusi's concluding argument that the Qur'anic miracle is its eloquence and that the challenge was specifically to produce a surah.

Core Idea
The Qur'an's miracle is its unique eloquence, proven by the challenge to bring a surah.

Sanusi wraps up the discussion on i'jaz by presenting the view he considers most sound. After examining multiple theories, he settles on eloquence as the definitive miracle of the Qur'an. He also confirms that the historical challenge was to produce a surah, grounding the basis of the miracle in a concrete test.

Guided Path
1
Understand the context
This passage is the conclusion of a debate on what constitutes the Qur'an's miraculous nature. Sanusi has systematically refuted other views before presenting his chosen position.
2
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Note the two key claims: the chosen miracle is eloquence, and the challenge was established by bringing a surah.
The passage begins with 'wa idha taqarrara' signaling a settled conclusion.
3
Reflect on 'al-mukhtar'
The term 'al-mukhtar' means 'the chosen view' – Sanusi’s preferred position after weighing the evidence. It is not arbitrary but the result of reasoned argument.
4
Consider the incomplete statement
The passage begins to quote 'some of the associates' but cuts off. Think about what they might have said: perhaps a qualification or additional support for the conclusion.
The ellipsis indicates the text is incomplete in the source.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا تقرر أن المعجز على المختار المتحدى به البلاغة (٢) ، وأنَّ التحدي قد استقر بالإتيان بسورة .. فقد قال بعضُ الأصحابِ : هذهِ
And when it is settled that the miracle according to what is chosen is the eloquence with which the challenge was made, and that the challenge has been established by bringing a surah... then some of the associates said: this...
Source pages p. 585

Commentary
This passage serves as the conclusion of the discussion on i'jaz. The author states that, after examining and refuting various opinions, it is now settled (taqarrara) that the miracle (al-mu'jiz), according to the chosen view (al-mukhtar), is al-balagha (eloquence) – the very thing with which the challenge was made. He also reaffirms that the challenge (tahaddi) was established by bringing a surah (or ten surahs). The text then begins to report a statement by some of the associates (ba'd al-ashab) but is cut off. The footnote clarifies that 'al-balagha' should be understood as 'its special style and its eloquence' (nazmuhu al-khas wa fasahatuhu). This ties back to the earlier lesson on the chosen view combining eloquence and style.

Key Terms
المختار
البلاغة
التحدي
الأصحاب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The conclusion that the miracle is eloquence is an arbitrary choice without reasoning.
Correction: Sanusi's conclusion is the result of systematic refutation of other views, as seen in the preceding lessons.

Checkpoint
According to the settled conclusion, what is the chosen basis of the Qur'anic miracle?
A) Its coherence
B) Its prophecies
C) Its eloquence (al-balagha)
D) Its eternity

Key Takeaway
Sanusi settles that the miracle of the Qur'an is its unique eloquence, and the challenge was to produce a surah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Qur'an's miracle is its eloquence—do you feel the weight of that challenge when you recite or hear the Qur'an? Are you struck by its unique beauty, or has familiarity dulled your heart? This week, read a short surah in Arabic and reflect on why no human can match it. What will you change in your daily recitation to truly sense its miraculous nature?
?
Sanusi settles a debate about the miracle, but the challenge remains open until the Day of Judgment. Have you ever truly accepted that challenge, or do you take the Qur'an's divinity for granted? If the Qur'an were to confront you personally with its eloquence, would you bow in submission or turn away?
?
The scholars concluded that eloquence is the miracle. Does your interaction with the Qur'an reflect that you believe it is beyond human capacity? Or do you treat it like any other book? Commit to memorizing and pondering the linguistic precision of one verse this week as an act of humility before its challenge.

Additional Proofs of Prophethood Beyond Miracles
Author lists additional proofs of prophethood beyond miracles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that prophethood is proven not only by miracles but also by the Prophet's innate perfections and divine confirmation.

Core Idea
The Prophet's character itself is a proof of his prophethood.

This passage expands the evidence for prophethood beyond the usual miracles. It points to the Prophet's own perfect nature and how even before his mission, his character declared his prophethood. Finally, it notes that God Himself confirmed his truthfulness by mentioning him in previous scriptures.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice how the author builds his case step by step.
2
Identify the three categories of proof
The passage presents three distinct proofs: miracles, innate perfections, and divine mention. Highlight each one.
The phrase 'ثم هذا إلى...' signals a new proof.
3
Reflect on the significance of character as proof
Consider why the Prophet's creation (khalaq) and character (khuluq) could be seen as evidence of prophethood even before his mission.
The perfections 'almost declared' his prophethood beforehand.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قرائن أخرى على ثبوت نبوته عليه الصلاة والسلام : ثم هذا إلى ما له مِنَ المعجزاتِ التي لا تُحصى ، ثم إلى ما جُبِلَتْ عليهِ ذاتُهُ الكريمةُ مِنَ الكمالاتِ التي كادَتْ أنْ تُفصِحَ - بل أفصحَتْ - قبلَ مبعثِهِ برسالتِهِ خَلْقاً وخُلْقاً ثم معَ ذلكَ كلّهِ : أَكَدَ اللهُ تعالى صدْقَهُ بذكرِهِ باسمِهِ
Other indications of the confirmation of his prophethood, peace be upon him: Then this, in addition to the miracles that cannot be counted, then in addition to what his noble essence was endowed with of perfections that almost declared – rather they declared – before his mission with his message, in creation and character; then with all of that, God Almighty confirmed his truthfulness by mentioning him by His name.
Source pages p. 591

Commentary
This passage is a listing of additional proofs for the Prophet's prophethood. It begins by stating that there are other indications (قرائن) beyond miracles. It mentions the countless miracles (المعجزات التي لا تحصى), then points to the Prophet's innate perfections (الكمالات) with which his noble essence (ذاته الكريمة) was endowed. These perfections were so apparent that they almost declared – indeed they did declare – his prophethood even before his mission, both in his physical creation (خلقاً) and his moral character (خلقاً). Finally, it notes that in addition to all this, God confirmed his truthfulness by mentioning him by His name (بذكرِهِ باسمِهِ) – likely a reference to the mention of Muhammad in previous scriptures or the shahada. The passage presents these as cumulative evidence supporting his prophethood.

Key Terms

نبوة
كمالات
خلقاً وخُلْقاً

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That only miracles prove prophethood.
Correction: This passage shows that the Prophet's character and perfections are also proofs, along with divine mention.

Checkpoint

B) His innate perfections in creation and character.
C) His military victories.
D) The number of his companions.

Key Takeaway
The evidence for the Prophet's prophethood includes his miracles, his perfect character, and God's confirmation through mentioning him by name.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

When you look at your own life before you fully committed to Islam, was there any sign that pointed to your eventual faith? How does that compare to the Prophet's pre-prophethood state?
?
God confirmed the Prophet's truthfulness by mentioning him by His name. Do you live in a way that your name is associated with truthfulness and faith? If not, what concrete step will you take today to make your name a testimony to your beliefs?

The Abundance of Prophetic Evidences
Sanusi lists multiple independent proofs for prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the multitude of independent proofs for the Prophet's prophethood, including his miracles, innate perfections, mention in scriptures, and divine measures to remove confusion.

Core Idea
The proofs for prophethood are so numerous that each alone suffices.

Sanusi continues to build the case for prophethood by listing additional evidences beyond the miracle of the Qur'an. He highlights that the Prophet's countless miracles, his perfect character, his mention in previous scriptures, and even the prevention of others from using his name all point to his truthfulness. This lesson surveys these proofs and shows how they converge.

Guided Path
1
Read the enumeration of proofs
Start by reading the Arabic passage from 'قرائن أخرى' to 'كيف وقد اجتمعت كلها فيه'. Notice the chain of evidence Sanusi presents.
The passage lists multiple proofs in rapid succession.
2
Identify each proof type
Identify each distinct proof: countless miracles, innate perfections, mention in past scriptures, testimony of scholars, prevention of name usage. Write them down.
3
Reflect on the significance of multiple proofs
Consider Sanusi's statement that each proof alone would be sufficient. Why does he emphasize their convergence?
The multiplicity strengthens certainty and removes doubts.
4
Connect to the broader argument
Think about how this list supports the overall claim of prophethood. How does it complement the earlier argument from the Qur'an's inimitability?

Other proofs for the affirmation of his prophethood, peace be upon him. Then this in addition to his countless miracles, then in addition to what his noble essence was endowed with of perfections that almost declared — rather, declared — before his mission with his message, in creation and character. Then, along with all of that, Allah Almighty confirmed his truthfulness by mentioning him by name and by all his attributes in the past scriptures. He said, exalted: 'Those who follow the Messenger, the unlettered Prophet...' [al-A‘raf 7:157] the verse. And He set free the tongues of the scholars close to his mission with all of that, until indeed He, glorified, by His grace, from what He confirmed to remove confusion about his prophethood, that He prevented the Arabs before him from being named with his specific name, except for a few people who were named close to his birth with his name hoping for prophethood to be for them, because they had heard it from the scholars. Commentary
This passage enumerates additional evidences for the Prophet Muhammad’s prophethood after having discussed the miracle of the Qur’an’s eloquence in previous sections. It begins by noting his countless miracles, then his innate perfections in creation and character which virtually proclaimed his prophethood before his mission. Then it mentions that Allah confirmed his truthfulness by mentioning him by name and attributes in previous scriptures, quoting part of Qur’an 7:157. Another evidence is that scholars near his time spoke openly about him. To remove all doubt, Allah prevented Arabs before him from using his specific name, except for a few who used it hoping to attain prophethood, but none of them actually claimed prophethood. The passage concludes that all these indicators are numerous, each sufficient alone, and they reduce to two ways: rational and transmitted. The rational way includes the miracle of the Qur’an’s eloquence (already discussed) and the fact that he foretold hidden things (though this is incomplete in the text).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that only the Qur'an's miracle is a sufficient proof for prophethood.
Correction: Sanusi shows that there are many independent proofs, each of which alone would be sufficient, and their convergence provides even stronger evidence.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, what is the significance of the fact that many proofs for prophethood exist?
A) They are all needed to make a convincing case.
B) Each proof alone is sufficient, and their convergence strengthens the evidence.
C) The proofs are only for scholars.
D) The proofs are only rational.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's prophethood is supported by numerous independent proofs, each sufficient alone, eliminating any doubt.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have learned that even the Prophet's innate character testified to his prophethood before his mission. Does your own character testify to your faith in him? What one specific mannerism or habit do you need to change today so that people see the light of Islam in you?
?
The Arabs were prevented from using his name to avoid confusion about who the true prophet is. Are there any actions or words of yours that cause confusion about your identity as a follower of Muhammad (ﷺ)? Will you commit to removing one source of confusion this week?
?
Multiple independent proofs exist, each sufficient to prove his prophethood. Yet many reject. Do you personally rely on all these proofs or just one? If a non-Muslim asked you to prove his prophethood with one of these proofs, could you do it confidently? Which proof will you study deeply starting today so that your certainty becomes unshakeable?

Prophethood
beginner
4 min
Classifying the Proofs and the First Rational Proof
Sanusi classifies proofs into rational and transmitted, then begins the rational proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi classifies proofs into rational and transmitted categories and the first rational proof from the Qur'an's inimitability.

Core Idea
Proofs for prophethood are either rational or transmitted; the Qur'an's eloquence is a rational proof.

After listing numerous specific signs, Sanusi now organizes them into two fundamental categories: rational proofs accessible to reason and transmitted proofs from scripture and tradition. He begins the rational proofs with the miracle of the Qur'an's eloquence, which he had previously discussed, and then starts to mention the second proof about foretelling hidden events, though the text is incomplete.

Guided Path
1
Understand the two categories
Read the passage that states proofs revert to two ways: rational and transmitted. Reflect on what each category means.
Rational proofs are based on reason; transmitted proofs rely on revelation and tradition.
2
Locate the first rational proof
Identify the first rational aspect: the miracle of the Qur'an's eloquence. Recall that Sanusi had discussed this earlier.
3
Note the incomplete second proof
The second rational proof about foretelling hidden events is cut off. Understand that the full argument is not available in this passage.
The source text ends mid-sentence, so we only have the beginning of this proof.
4
See how classification aids argumentation
Think about why Sanusi divides proofs this way. How does it strengthen the overall case?
Classification shows comprehensiveness and appeals to different types of evidence.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قرائن أخرى على ثبوت نبوته عليه الصلاة والسلام ﴿١﴾ ثم هذا إلى ما له مِنَ المعجزات التي لا تُحصى ، ثم إلى ما جُبِلَتْ عليهِ ذاتُهُ الكريمةُ مِنَ الكمالاتِ التي كادَتْ أنْ تُفصِحَ - بل أفصحَتْ - قبلَ مبعثِهِ برسالتِهِ خَلْقاً وخُلْقاً ثم معَ ذلكَ كلّهِ : أَكَدَ اللهُ تعالى صدْقَهُ بذكرِهِ باسمِهِ وبجميع وصفِهِ في الكتب الماضية ، قال تعالى : ﴿ الَّذِينَ يَتَّبِعُونَ الرَّسُولَ النَّبِيَّ الْأُمّى ... ﴾ [الأعراف : ١٥٧] الآية . وأطلق ألسنة الأحبار قريباً مِنْ مبعثه بجميع ذلك حتى إِنَّهُ سبحانَهُ بفضلِهِ ممَّا أَكَّدَ بِهِ زوالَ اللَّبْسِ عن نبوتِهِ أن منع العرب قبلَهُ مِنَ التسمّي باسمِهِ الخاص بهِ ، إلا أُناساً قليلين تسموا قريباً مِنْ مولدِهِ باسمه رجاءَ حصولِ النبوة لهم ؛ لما سمعوهُ مِنَ الأحبارِ ، ثم مِنْ عظيم فضلِ اللهِ تعالى في إزالة اللَّبْس : أن لم يطلق لسان أحدٍ مِنْ أولئك الذين تسموا باسمِهِ بدعوى النبوَّةِ . يعني : أنَّ الدال على نبوَّةِ نبينا ومولانا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ أشياء كثيرة ، كلُّ واحدٍ منها يصلحُ لأن يكون دليلاً مستقلاً لو انفرد ، كيف وقدِ اجتمعَتْ كلُّها فيه ؟! ومرجعها إلى طريقين : عقلي ، ونقلي . أما العقلي فوجوه : أحدها : معجزةُ بلاغة القرآن على ما سبق (۲) وثانيها : أنَّهُ صَلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ أخبرَ المغيَّبات ، فطابقت
Other proofs for the affirmation of his prophethood, peace be upon him. Then this in addition to his countless miracles, then in addition to what his noble essence was endowed with of perfections that almost declared — rather, declared — before his mission with his message, in creation and character. Then, along with all of that, Allah Almighty confirmed his truthfulness by mentioning him by name and by all his attributes in the past scriptures. He said, exalted: 'Those who follow the Messenger, the unlettered Prophet...' [al-A‘raf 7:157] the verse. And He set free the tongues of the scholars close to his mission with all of that, until indeed He, glorified, by His grace, from what He confirmed to remove confusion about his prophethood, that He prevented the Arabs before him from being named with his specific name, except for a few people who were named close to his birth with his name hoping for prophethood to be for them, because they had heard it from the scholars. Then, from the great grace of Allah Almighty in removing confusion: that He did not set free the tongue of any of those who were named with his name with a claim to prophethood. Meaning: that the indicators of the prophethood of our Prophet and master Muhammad, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, are many things, each one of which is suitable to be an independent proof if it were alone; how when all of them have gathered in him?! Their referent is two ways: rational and transmitted. As for the rational, it has aspects: one of them is the miracle of the eloquence of the Qur’an according to what preceded. The second is that he, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, informed of hidden things, and they corresponded...

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that rational and transmitted proofs are mutually exclusive or contradictory.
Correction: Sanusi presents them as complementary categories that together provide comprehensive evidence.

Checkpoint
Into how many categories does Sanusi divide the proofs for prophethood?
A) Three categories.
B) Two categories: rational and transmitted.
C) One category: rational only.
D) Four categories: rational, transmitted, historical, and empirical.

Key Takeaway
Proofs for prophethood are classified into rational and transmitted, and the first rational proof is the miracle of the Qur'an's eloquence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Sanusi begins with the miracle of the Qur'an's eloquence as the first rational proof. When was the last time you sat with the Arabic text of the Qur'an and let its beauty strike you—not just its meaning—so that your faith in the Prophet grew? Will you commit to doing that this week?
?
The lesson says rational proofs can be verified by reason. Is your belief in the Prophet ﷺ more anchored in rational conviction or in inherited tradition? If you had to defend it rationally, could you? What would you need to learn?
?
The second rational proof is the Prophet's foretelling of hidden events that came true. Have you ever studied any of those prophecies in detail? Pick one prophecy mentioned in the Qur'an or hadith, and before next week, verify its fulfillment. How would that affect your certainty?
